The Preemptor's Options When the Buyer Builds or Plants
Ruling with hadith proof on buyer's building/planting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the preemptor when the buyer builds or plants on the sold property without permission, and explain the hadith proof for this ruling.

Core Idea
The preemptor may take at demolition value or compel removal—he is not forced to pay for unauthorized improvements.

In pre-emption (shuf'a), the buyer may make improvements to the property after the sale but before the preemptor takes possession. This lesson examines the ruling when the buyer builds or plants without the preemptor's permission. The Hanafi school grants the preemptor a choice, based on a hadith and a companion saying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The buyer builds a structure or plants trees on the sold property after the sale but before the preemptor exercises his right. This act is done without the preemptor's permission.
The act must be voluntary and without permission; if with permission, the ruling changes.
2
State the preemptor's options
The preemptor has two options: (1) take the property at the original price plus the value of the building/plants as if they were to be removed (demolition value), or (2) compel the buyer to remove the building/plants at the buyer's own expense.
The phrase 'مَقْلُوعًا' means 'uprooted' or 'as demolished'.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Aisha (RA) narrated in Sunan al-Bayhaqi, and a companion saying from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA). Both distinguish between building with permission (entitling the builder to the full value) and building without permission (entitling only to the demolition materials).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but clear in meaning (qati al-dalala).
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's operative phrase is the distinction between 'with permission' and 'without permission'. The buyer did not have the preemptor's permission, so the buyer only gets the physical materials (naqd), not the standing value. This directly supports the preemptor's option to take at demolition value or compel removal.
The companion saying confirms the same principle.
5
Note the thamarah
The practical consequence is that the preemptor is not forced to pay for improvements he did not authorize. If the improvements are valuable to him, he may pay only the salvage value; otherwise, he can have them removed at the buyer's cost.
Some other schools may differ on this point, but the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا بَنَى الْمُشْتَرِي، أَوْ غَرَسَ ثُمَّ قَضَى لِلشَّفِيعِ بِالشُّفْعَةِ فَهُوَ بِاخْيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهَا بِالثَّمَنِ وَقِيمَةِ الْبِنَاءِ، وَالْغَرْسِ مَقْلُوعًا، وَإِنْ شَاءَ كُلَّفَ الْمُشْتَرِي قَلْعَهُ
٢٣ وَإِذَا أَخَذَهَا الشَّفِيعُ فَبَى فِيهَا، أَوْ غَرَسَ، ثُمَّ اسْتُحِقَّتْ رَجَعَ بِالثَّمَنِ وَلَا يَرْجِعُ بِقِيمَةِ الْبِنَاءِ، وَالْغَرْسِ
وَإِذَا انْهَدَمَتْ الدَّارُ، أَوْ احْتَرَقَ بِنَاؤُهَا، أَوْ جَفَّ شَجَرُ الْبُسْتَانِ بِغَيْرِ فِعْلِ أَحَدٍ فَالشَّفِيعُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ بِجَمِيعِ الثَّمَنِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ
وَإِنْ نَقَضَ الْمُشْتَرِي الْبِنَاءَ قِيلَ لِلشَّفِيعِ إِنْ شِئْت فَخُذْ الْعَرْصَةَ بِحِصَّتِهَا، وَإِنْ شِنْت فَدَعْ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ النِّقْضَ ۲۵
وَمَنْ ابْتَاعَ أَرْضًا، وَفِي تَخْلِهَا ثَمَرٌ أَخَذَهَا الشَّفِيعُ بِثَمَرِهَا فَإِنْ جَدَّهُ الْمُشْتَرِي سَقَطَ عَنْ الشَّفِيع حِصَّتُهُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا بَنَى الْمُشْتَرِي، أَوْ غَرَسَ 
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ هِي قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " مَنْ بَنَى فِي رِبَاعِ قَوْمِ بِإِذْنِهِمْ فَلَهُ الْقِيمَةُ، وَمَنْ بَنَى بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِمْ فَلَهُ النَّقْضُ "،(السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ بَنَى أَوْ غَرَسَ فِي أَرْضِ غَيْرِهِ، نمبر 11492)
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا بَنَى الْمُشْتَرِي، أَوْ غَرَسَ 
اعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: " مَنْ بَنَى فِي أَرْضِ قَوْمِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْهِمْ فَلَهُ نَقْضُهُ، وَإِنْ بَنَى بِإِذْنِهِمْ فَلَهُ قِيمَتُهُ، السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ بَغَ أَوْ غَرَسَ فِي أَرْضِ غَيْرِهِ، نمبر 11488)
۲۳ اصول: اگر شفعہ میں دوسرے کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور اسکی اجازت کے بغیر گھر بنالیا یا باغ لگایا تو اس کو توڑنے کا حکم ہو گا۔
۲۵ اصول : زمین سے کوئی شی متصل ہو، اور اس کے تابع ہو تو زمین کے ساتھ اس میں بھی حق شفعہ ہو گا۔
And if the buyer builds or plants, then the preemptor is decreed the pre-emption, he has an option: if he wishes, he takes the property with the price and the value of the building and the plants as uprooted; and if he wishes, the buyer is compelled to remove them. (23) And if the preemptor takes it and then builds or plants upon it, then it is found to have been usurped, he recovers the price but does not recover the value of the building and plants. And if the house collapses, or its building burns, or the trees of the garden dry up without any person’s action, the preemptor has an option: if he wishes, he takes it with the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves. And if the buyer demolishes the building, it is said to the preemptor: ‘If you wish, take the land with its share, and if you wish, leave; and he may not take the demolished materials.’ (25) And whoever buys land, and on its palm trees there is fruit, the preemptor takes it with its fruit. If the buyer picks it, the preemptor’s share of it falls. Evidence: (1) The hadith for the ruling ‘when the buyer builds or plants’ from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Whoever builds on the lands of a people with their permission, he gets the value; and whoever builds without their permission, he gets the demolition.” (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on who builds or plants in another’s land, no. 11492). Evidence: (2) The Companion’s saying from Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) who said: “Whoever builds in the land of a people without their permission, he gets his demolition; and if he builds with their permission, he gets its value.” (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on who builds or plants in another’s land, no. 11488). Principle (23): If in pre-emption another’s right becomes attached and without his permission a house is built or a garden planted, then he will be commanded to demolish it. Principle (25): Whatever is connected to the land and is subordinate to it, the pre-emption right applies to it along with the land.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings regarding alterations to the property after sale but before the preemptor takes possession. It begins with the buyer’s building or planting after the sale. When the preemptor wins his case, he has an option: either to take the property at the original price plus the value of the building and plants as if they were to be removed (i.e., their value as demolished/dug up, not standing), or to compel the buyer to remove them at his own cost. This follows the principle that the buyer built or planted without the preemptor’s permission, so the preemptor is not forced to pay for improvements he did not authorize. The hadith from Aisha (RA) and the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (RA) support this: one who builds on another’s land with permission gets compensation for the value; without permission, he can only take the physical materials (nuqd). Then comes the case of the preemptor himself building or planting after taking the property, but later the property is found to have been usurped from the original seller (i.e., the seller did not own it). In that case, the preemptor recovers the price he paid but not the value of his improvements, because he built at his own risk on a property that was not lawfully his. Next, natural destruction: if the building collapses, burns, or trees dry up without anyone’s act, the preemptor can still take the property at the full price or leave it—because the sale contract was valid and the price was established, the risk of accidental loss falls on the buyer (who owned the property until the preemptor takes it). The preemptor is not forced to pay for something he didn't receive. If the buyer voluntarily demolishes the building, the preemptor can either take the land at its proportionate share of the price or leave it; he cannot take the demolished materials because they are not part of the land. Finally, if land with fruit on trees is sold, the preemptor takes it with the fruit. If the buyer picks the fruit before the preemptor takes possession, the fruit belongs to the buyer, and the preemptor’s share of the price for the fruit falls accordingly. The usul notes explain: (23) the principle that unauthorized building on another’s right bearer must be removed; (25) that anything attached to land and subordinate to it is included in the pre-emption right.

Key Terms
نَقْض (naqd): Demolished materials (bricks, wood, etc.) of a building; also used for the act of demolition.
قَلْع (qal'): The act of uprooting or removing a building or plants from the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what does the preemptor pay if he chooses to take the property with the buyer's building?
A) The original price only
B) The original price plus the full standing value of the building
C) The original price plus the value of the building as demolished
D) Nothing, because the buyer built without permission

Key Takeaway
The preemptor may take the property at the price plus demolition value or compel removal, based on the hadith distinction between building with and without permission.

Other Changes to Pre-empted Property: Preemptor's Building, Natural Destruction, Buyer Demolition, and Fruit
Rulings on various changes to pre-empted property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the following scenarios: preemptor builds/plants, natural destruction, buyer demolishes, and fruit on trees.

Core Idea
The preemptor's rights adjust based on who caused the change and whether it was with permission or natural.

The previous lesson dealt with the buyer's building or planting. This lesson covers other situations: the preemptor's own improvements, accidental destruction, buyer's demolition, and fruit on trees. Each has a distinct ruling based on risk allocation and the status of the property.

Guided Path
1
Preemptor builds/plants on usurped property
If the preemptor, after taking possession, builds or plants, and later the property is found to have been usurped (seller not owner), the preemptor recovers only the price paid, not the value of his improvements. He built at his own risk.
This is because the property was not lawfully owned by the seller, so the preemptor's title is defective.
2
Natural destruction
If the building collapses, burns, or trees dry up without human action, the preemptor may either take the property at the full price or leave it. The risk of accidental loss falls on the buyer during the interim period.
The preemptor is not forced to pay for something that has been destroyed through no one's fault.
3
Buyer demolishes the building
If the buyer voluntarily demolishes the building, the preemptor can only take the land (the 'arsa') at its proportionate share of the price, or he may leave the pre-emption entirely. He cannot take the demolished materials.
The demolished materials are not part of the land and are considered the buyer's property.
4
Fruit on trees
If the land has fruit on its trees at the time of sale, the preemptor takes the property including the fruit. If the buyer picks the fruit before the preemptor takes possession, the fruit belongs to the buyer, and the preemptor's share of the price for the fruit is deducted.
The usul principle states that anything attached to the land and subordinate to it is included in the pre-emption right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage presents several rulings regarding alterations to the property after sale but before the preemptor takes possession. It begins with the buyer’s building or planting after the sale. When the preemptor wins his case, he has an option: either to take the property at the original price plus the value of the building and plants as if they were to be removed (i.e., their value as demolished/dug up, not standing), or to compel the buyer to remove them at his own cost. This follows the principle that the buyer built or planted without the preemptor’s permission, so the preemptor is not forced to pay for improvements he did not authorize. The hadith from Aisha (RA) and the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (RA) support this: one who builds on another’s land with permission gets compensation for the value; without permission, he can only take the physical materials (nuqd). Then comes the case of the preemptor himself building or planting after taking the property, but later the property is found to have been usurped from the original seller (i.e., the seller did not own it). In that case, the preemptor recovers the price he paid but not the value of his improvements, because he built at his own risk on a property that was not lawfully his. Next, natural destruction: if the building collapses, burns, or trees dry up without anyone’s act, the preemptor can still take the property at the full price or leave it—because the sale contract was valid and the price was established, the risk of accidental loss falls on the buyer (who owned the property until the preemptor takes it). The preemptor is not forced to pay for something he didn't receive. If the buyer voluntarily demolishes the building, the preemptor can either take the land at its proportionate share of the price or leave it; he cannot take the demolished materials because they are not part of the land. Finally, if land with fruit on trees is sold, the preemptor takes it with the fruit. If the buyer picks the fruit before the preemptor takes possession, the fruit belongs to the buyer, and the preemptor’s share of the price for the fruit falls accordingly. The usul notes explain: (23) the principle that unauthorized building on another’s right bearer must be removed; (25) that anything attached to land and subordinate to it is included in the pre-emption right.

Key Terms
نَقْض (naqd): Demolished materials (bricks, wood, etc.) of a building; also used for the act of demolition.
عَرْصَة (arsa): The land or site of a building without the structure.
ثَمَر (thamar): Fruit on trees (date palms in this context).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the buyer demolishes the building on the pre-empted property, what can the preemptor do?
A) Take the demolished materials only
B) Take the land at its share of the price
C) Take the full property at the original price as if nothing happened
D) Force the buyer to rebuild

Key Takeaway
The preemptor's options change based on the nature of the change: natural destruction, buyer's demolition, fruit picking, and his own building on usurped property each have distinct rulings.

Preemptor's Options After Decree: Sight, Defect, Credit, Division, and Return
Rulings on preemptor's options after judge's decree plus proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preemptor's options after a judge's decree and apply the conditions that affect their validity.

Core Idea
A preemptor's right revives if the sale is annulled without a judge's decree or by mutual rescission.

This passage outlines several scenarios after a judge awards property to a preemptor. It covers the preemptor's right to inspect the property (option of sight), return it for defects even if the buyer waived immunity, and choose between cash or deferred payment. It also explains when division eliminates pre-emption and when a waiver can be revived. These rulings protect the preemptor from being forced into an unfair sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preemptor's options
List the three options: sight, defect, and credit payment. Understand that these are rights (mubah), not obligations.
2
Understand the effect of buyer's stipulations
The preemptor is not bound by the buyer's waiver of defects; he retains the option of defect even if the buyer waived it.
3
Analyze the division scenario
When co-owners divide the property (qisma), no pre-emption applies among them because joint ownership ends.
4
Examine waiver and its revival
If the preemptor waives his right and later the buyer returns the property by judicial decree, the waiver stands. But if the return is non-judicial or by mutual rescission (taqayul), the preemptor's right revives.
5
Connect the hadith proofs
The hadith on option of sight (Abu Hurairah) directly supports khiyar al-ru'ya. The hadith 'kharaj bi-daman' supports that the buyer bears risk and can keep profits, but the preemptor still has the option of defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلشَّفِيعِ بِالدَّارِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ رَآهَا فَلَهُ خِيَارُ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَإِنْ وَجَدَ بِمَا عَيْبًا فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهَا، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُشْتَرِي شَرَطَ الْبَرَاءَةَ مِنْهُ ۲۷
وَإِذَا ابْتَاعَ بِثَمَنٍ مُؤَجَّلٍ فَالشَّفِيعُ بِالخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهَا بِثَمَنٍ حَالٍ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَبَرَ حَتَّى يَنْقَضِيَ الْأَجَلُ، ثُمَّ يَأْخُذَهَا وَإِذَا قَسَمَ الشُرَكَاءُ الْعَقَارَ فَلَا شُفْعَةَ خَارِهِمْ بِالْقِسْمَةِ
۲۸ وَإِذَا اشْتَرَى دَارًا فَسَلَّمَ الشَّفِيعُ الشُّفْعَةَ، ثُمَّ رَدَّهَا الْمُشْتَرِي بِخِيَارِ رُؤْيَةٍ، أَوْ شَرْطٍ، أَوْ عَيْبٍ بِقَضَاءِ قَاضٍ فَلَا شُفْعَةَ لَهُ وَإِنْ رَدَّهَا بِغَيْرِ قَضَاءِ قَاضِ، أَوْ تَقَايَلَا فَلِلشَّفِيعِ الشُّفْعَةُ
٢٦ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلشَّفِيعِ بِالدَّارِ 
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: مَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا لَمْ يَرَهُ فَهُوَ بِالْخِيَارِ إِذَا رَآهُ»، (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع نمبر 2805/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَيْنِ الْغَائِبَةِ، غمبر 10426 
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلشَّفِيعِ بِالدَّارِ 
اعَنْ عَائِشَةَ ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا، ابْتَاعَ غُلَامًا فَأَقَامَ عِنْدَهُ مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ أَنْ يُقِيمَ، ثُمَّ وَجَدَ بِهِ عَيْبًا فَخَاصَمَهُ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَرَدَّهُ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ الرَّجُلُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، قَدِ اسْتَغَلَّ غُلَامِي، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الحَرَاجُ بِالضَّمَانِ» »، ( سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابٌ فِيمَنِ اشْتَرَى عَبْدًا فَاسْتَعْمَلَهُ ثُمَّ وَجَدَ بِهِ عَيْبًا نمبر 3510)
اصول: شفعہ میں خیار عیب اور خیار رویت دونوں کا اختیار رہتا ہے، حتی کہ مشتری نے خیار رویت و عیب سے براءت کا اظہار کر دیا تب بھی شفیع کا خیار باقی رہے گا۔
اصول: ادھار لینے اور دینے کا معاملہ بائع اور مشتری کے اعتمادا اور رضامندی پر ہے۔
And if the judge decrees the house for the preemptor, and he had not seen it, he has the option of sight; and if he finds a defect in it, he may return it, even if the buyer had stipulated immunity from it. (27) And if he bought with a deferred price, the preemptor has an option: if he wishes, he takes it with an immediate price; and if he wishes, he waits until the term expires, then takes it. And if the partners divide the real estate, there is no pre-emption among them due to division. (28) And if he buys a house and the preemptor waives the pre-emption, then the buyer returns it due to an option of sight, condition, or defect by a judge’s decree, then there is no pre-emption for him. And if he returns it without a judge’s decree, or they mutually rescind, then the preemptor has the pre-emption. Evidence: (1) The hadith for the ruling ‘when the judge decrees the house for the preemptor’: from Abu Hurairah (RA), he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it.” (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Sales, no. 2805 / Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who permit sale of an unseen object, no. 10426). Evidence: (2) The hadith for the ruling: from Aisha (RA), that a man bought a slave and kept him as long as Allah willed, then found a defect in him and brought his case to the Prophet (peace be upon him), who returned him to the seller. The man said: O Messenger of Allah, he utilized my slave. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Profit follows liability.” (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the one who buys a slave and uses him then finds a defect, no. 3510). Principle: In pre-emption, both the option of defect and the option of sight remain; even if the buyer has declared immunity from the options of sight and defect, the preemptor’s option remains. Principle: The transaction of credit (lending and borrowing) is based on trust and consent between seller and buyer.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage covers the preemptor’s rights after the judge has decreed the property to him. First, if the preemptor has not seen the property, he retains the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'ya): he may inspect it and then accept or reject. This is proven by the hadith that a buyer who buys an unseen object has the option upon seeing. Second, if he finds a defect, he may return the property even if the original buyer waived immunity—because the preemptor is not bound by the buyer’s stipulations; he takes the property as it was at the time of sale. Third, if the original sale was on credit, the preemptor can either pay the full price immediately or wait until the credit term ends to take the property; he cannot be forced to take it on credit if he prefers cash. Fourth, if the co-partners divide the property (qisma), no pre-emption applies among them because division removes the joint ownership. Fifth, if a preemptor waives his right and then the buyer returns the property to the seller through a judge (e.g., due to defect), the preemptor’s waiver stands and he does not get a new right. But if the buyer returns it without a judge’s decree (e.g., by mutual agreement) or they mutually rescind (taqayul), the preemptor’s right revives because the sale is effectively annulled. The hadiths cited: the first supports the option of sight; the second (kharaj bi-daman) supports the idea that the buyer bears the risk and therefore keeps profits from the property during his ownership. The usul notes explain that the preemptor still has options even if the buyer stipulated immunity, and that credit is based on trust.

Key Terms
خِيَارُ الرُّؤْيَةِ (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option to cancel a sale after seeing the purchased object if it was unseen at the time of contract.
تَقَايُل (taqayul): Mutual rescission (iqala) where both parties agree to cancel the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the preemptor waives his right and later the buyer and seller mutually rescind the sale (taqayul), what is the preemptor's status?
A) His waiver is permanent; he has no right.
B) He has a new right of pre-emption on the same property.
C) He can only claim if the price is lower.
D) He can claim only if he pays a penalty.

Key Takeaway
Preemptor's rights are not extinguished by a simple waiver if the underlying sale is later undone without a judicial decree.

Two Types of Agency Contracts and Their Legal Effects
Classification of agency into two categories based on attribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify agency contracts into two types based on how the agent attributes the contract and apply the Hanafi rule to determine which rights attach to the agent versus the principal.

Core Idea
When an agent acts in his own name, he bears the rights and duties; when he acts in the principal's name, the principal bears them.

This lesson explores the Hanafi classification of agency into two categories. The crucial distinction is whether the agent attributes the contract to himself or to the principal. This determines who bears the legal consequences—an insight that resolves many practical disputes, especially in sales and marriages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on agency
The Hanafi school divides agency contracts into two types based on how the agent attributes the contract. Identify the two types and their respective legal effects as stated in the matn.
The text explicitly contrasts contracts like sale (self-attribution) and marriage (principal-attribution).
2
Recognize the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all rights and duties of an agency contract attach to the principal because ownership belongs to the principal. Compare this with the Hanafi position.
The opposition is based on the principle of ownership (milk).
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
The Hanafi argument is rational: the agent is the actual party performing the contract, so effects should attach to him. Also, hadith evidence supports agency in marriage and purchase. Examine the hadith cited in the text.
The hadith of Umm Salamah and the woman offering herself in marriage are used to show agency in marriage.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection
The Hanafi response differentiates between contracts where the agent acts in his own name vs. the principal's name. In the former, the agent is the direct party; in the latter, the principal is the direct party.
This response shows why rights attach to the agent in sale but to the principal in marriage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: In a sale, the buyer must sue the agent for defects, not the principal. In marriage, the agent cannot be sued for dower. Identify the practical impact in real life.
This distinction is critical for litigation and contract enforcement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْوَكَالَةِ وَالْعُقُودُ الَّتِي يَعْقِدُهَا الْوَكَلَاءُ عَلَى ضَرْبَيْنِ كُلُّ عَقْدٍ يُضِيفُهُ الْوَكِيلُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ مِثْلُ الْبَيْعِ وَالْإِجَارَةِ فَحُقُوقُ ذَلِكَ الْعَقْدِ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْوَكِيلِ دُونَ الْمُوَكَّلِ فَيُسَلِّمُ الْمَبِيعَ وَيَقْبِضُ الثَّمَنَ وَيُطَالِبُ بِالثَّمَنِ إِذَا اشْتَرَى وَيَقْبِضُ الْمَبِيعَ وَيُخَاصِمُ فِي الْعَيْبِ وَكُلُّ عَقْدٍ يُضِيفُهُ إِلَى مُوَكِّلِهِ كَالنِّكَاحِ وَالْخُلْعِ وَالصُّلْحِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمْدِ فَإِنَّ حُقُوقَهُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمُوَكَّلِ دُونَ الْوَكِيلِ فَلَا يُطَالِبُ وَكِيلُ الزَّوْجِ بِالصَّدَاقِ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ وَكِيلَ الْمَرْأَةِ تَسْلِيمُهَا وَإِذَا طَالَبَ الْمُوَكَّلُ الْمُشْتَرِيَ بِالثَّمَنِ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَمْنَعَهُ إِيَّاهُ فَإِنْ دَفَعَهُ إِلَيْهِ جَازَ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْوَكِيلِ أَنْ يُطَالِبَهُ بِهِ ثَانِيًا

ووجه : (٢) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَإِنْ وَكَلَا صَبِيًّا مَحْجُورًا عَلَيْهِ يَعْقِلُ الْبَيْعَ عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ : «لَمَّا انْقَضَتْ عِدَّتُهَا ...... وَأَمَّا قَوْلُكِ: أَنْ لَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَوْلِيَائِي شَاهِدٌ، فَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَوْلِيَائِكِ شَاهِدٌ وَلَا غَائِبٌ يَكْرَهُ ذَلِكَ. فَقَالَتْ لِابْنِهَا : يَا عُمَرُ، قُمْ فَزَوِّجْ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَزَوَّجَهُ». (سنن نسائي إِنْكَاحُ الابْنِ أُمَّهُ، نمبر 3254)

و وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ عَقْدِ يُضِيفُهُ إِلَى مُوَكِّلِهِ كَالنِكَاحِ: سَمِعْتُ سَهْلَ بْنَ سَعْدٍ السَّاعِدِيَّ يَقُولُ: «إِنِّي لَفِي الْقَوْمِ عِنْدَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذْ قَامَتِ امْرَأَةٌ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ....... فَقَالَ : هَلْ مَعَكَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ شَيْءٍ؟ قَالَ: مَعِي سُورَةُ كَذَا وَسُورَةُ كَذَا، قَالَ: اذْهَبْ فَقَدْ أَنْكَحْتُكَهَا بِمَا مَعَكَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ.» ( بخاري شريف ، بَابُ التَّزْوِيجِ عَلَى الْقُرْآنِ وَبِغَيْرِ صَدَاقٍ،نمرب،5149)

فَأَتَاهُ بِدِينَارٍ بِشَاةٍ وَدِينَارٍ

ال وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا لِيَشْتَرِيَ لَهُ شَيْئًا عَنْ عُرْوَةَ يَعْنِي ابْنَ أَبِي الْجَعْدِ الْبَارِقِيَّ، قَالَ: «أَعْطَاهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم دِينَارًا يَشْتَرِي بِهِ أُضْحِيَّةً، أَوْ شَاةً فَاشْتَرَى شَاتَيْنِ فَبَاعَ إِحْدَاهُمَا فَدَعَا لَهُ بِالْبَرَكَةِ فِي بَيْعِهِ كَانَ لَوِ اشْتَرَى تُرَابًا لَرَبِحَ فِيهِ»،(سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْمُضَارِبِ يُخَالِفُ ، 3384/سنن الترمذي، باب الشراء والبيع الموقوفين، 1258)

اصول : حنفیہ: وکیل حقیقت میں اور حکما عقد کرتا ہے، اس لئے حقوق بھی وکیل کیساتھ متعلق ہوں گے۔ اصول: امام شافعی: ملکیت موکل کی ہے اسلئے حقوق بھی موکل کیسا تھ متعلق ہوں گے۔
The Book of Agency: The contracts that agents make are of two types. Every contract that the agent attributes to himself, such as sale and lease, its rights pertain to the agent, not the principal. So he delivers the sold item, receives the price, demands the price if he bought, receives the sold item, and litigates regarding defects. And every contract that he attributes to his principal, such as marriage, khul', and compromise for intentional homicide, its rights pertain to the principal, not the agent. So the agent of the husband does not demand the dower, and the agent of the woman is not obliged to hand her over. And when the principal demands the price from the buyer, he has the right to withhold it from him. If he pays it to him, it is valid, and the agent cannot demand it a second time. [Then hadith evidence and usul note: Hanafi: The agent performs the contract in reality and by legal fiction, so rights also attach to the agent. Shafi'i: Ownership belongs to the principal, so rights also attach to the principal.]
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage from Al-Quduri with commentary. The matn establishes that agency contracts fall into two categories: those where the agent acts in his own name (e.g., sale, lease) and those where he acts in the principal's name (e.g., marriage, khul'). In the first category, legal rights and duties attach to the agent, so he delivers the goods, receives payment, and can sue for defects. In the second, rights attach to the principal, so the agent cannot claim the dower or be required to hand over the wife. The commentary then provides hadith proofs for the validity of agency in marriage (Umm Salamah's case and the woman who offered herself in marriage) and for general purchase agency (the hadith of Urwah about buying an udhiya). The usul note contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i principles: Hanafis see the agent as the real and legal contractor, while Shafi'is see the principal as the true owner. This difference leads to the practical consequences mentioned. The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): A contract by which one person authorizes another to act on his behalf in a permissible matter.
وكيل (wakīl): The person authorized to act on behalf of another (the principal).
موكل (muwakkil): The person who authorizes the agent to act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale where the agent acts in his own name, who is responsible for delivering the goods and receiving the price?
A) The principal
B) The agent
C) Both equally
D) The buyer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes agency contracts based on attribution: self-reference attaches rights to the agent, principal-reference attaches rights to the principal.

Specifying the Purchase in Agency
Rulings on specification of purchase and return of defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of specifying the genus and description (or genus and price) for a purchase agency, identify when a general agency suffices, and apply the agent's right to return defective goods before and after delivery to the principal.

Core Idea
An agent must know exactly what to buy unless the principal grants full discretion — and the agent may return defects only while in possession.

This passage from Al-Quduri lays out the fundamental rules for a purchase agency. The principal must clearly specify the item to be bought—either by its type and quality, or by its type and price—unless a general agency is given. Additionally, the agent has the right to return defective goods as long as they remain in his custody; once delivered to the principal, the agent loses that right without permission. These rules protect both parties from ambiguity and ensure the agency fulfills its purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core requirement for a purchase agency
Find the Arabic phrase that states the necessity of specifying the item. Note the two alternatives: genus+description or genus+price.
The text uses 'فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَسْمِيَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَصِفَتِهِ أَوْ جِنْسِهِ وَمَبْلَعِهِ'.
2
Recognize the exception of general agency
Look for the condition that avoids the specification requirement: a general agency (wakālah ʿāmmah) where the principal says 'buy whatever you see.'
The text says 'إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُ وَكَالَةً عَامَّةً فَيَقُولَ لَهُ ابْتَعْ لِي مَا رَأَيْت'.
3
Understand the agent's right to return defective goods
Note that after purchase and receipt, if the agent discovers a defect, he may return the item. But this right is conditional: the goods must still be in his possession.
The text says 'فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ بِالْعَيْبِ مَا دَامَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ'.
4
Distinguish the rule after delivery to the principal
Once the agent hands over the goods to the principal, he cannot return them without the principal's explicit permission.
The text says 'فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا لِيَشْتَرِيَ لَهُ شَيْئًا فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَسْمِيَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَصِفَتِهِ أَوْ جِنْسِهِ وَمَبْلَعِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُ وَكَالَةً عَامَّةً فَيَقُولَ لَهُ ابْتَعْ لِي مَا رَأَيْت

فَإِذَا اشْتَرَى الْوَكِيلُ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ ثُمَّ اطَّلَعَ عَلَى عَيْبٍ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ بِالْعَيْبِ مَا دَامَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ

وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَمِ فَإِنْ فَارَقَ الْوَكِيلُ صَاحِبَهُ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ وَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ مُفَارَقَةُ الْمُوَكِّلِ

وَإِذَا دَفَعَ الْوَكِيلُ بِالشِّرَاءِ الثَّمَنَ مِنْ مَالِهِ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ

فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُوَكِّلِ وَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ الثَّمَنُ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ فَإِنْ حَبَسَهُ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ كَانَ مَضْمُونًا ضَمَانَ الرَّهْنِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَضَمَانَ الْمَبِيعِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ

وَإِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ رَجُلَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيمَا وُكِّلَا فِيهِ دُونَ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُمَا بِالْخُصُومَةِ أَوْ بِطَلَاقِ زَوْجَتِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِعِتْقِ عَبْدِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِرَدِّ وَدِيعَةٍ أَوْ عَارِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَصْبٍ أَوْ بِقَضَاءِ دَيْنٍ

قَالَ: «كُنتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَفَرٍ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمْنَا الْمَدِينَةَ، قَالَ: يَا بِلَالُ، اقْضِهِ وَزِدْهُ، فَأَعْطَاهُ أَرْبَعَةَ دَنَانِيرَ وَزَادَهُ قِيرَاطًا، بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ أَنْ يُعْطِيَ شَيْئًا وَلَمْ يبين، غبر، 2309)

وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَم: وَقَدْ وَكَّلَ عُمَرُ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ فِي الصَّرْفِ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْوَكَالَةِ فِي الصَّرْفِ وَالْمِيزَانِ، نمبر 2302)

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ «وَكَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِحِفْظِ زَكَاةِ رَمَضَانَ فَأَتَانِي آتٍ فَجَعَلَ يَحْنُو مِنَ الطَّعَامِ فَأَخَذْتُهُ وَقُلْتُ وَاللَّهِ لأَرْفَعَنَّكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِنِّي مُحْتَاجٌ وَعَلَيَّ عِيَالٌ وَلِي حَاجَةٌ شَدِيدَةٌ قَالَ فَخَلَّيْتُ عَنْهُ،، (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا فَتَرَكَ الْوَكِيلُ شَيْئًا فَأَجَازَهُ الْمُوَكَّلُ، نمبر، 2311)

وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: الْمُضَارِبُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، وَإِنْ تَعَدَّى أَمْرَكَ، » مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ: ضَمَانُ الْمُقَارَضِ إِذَا تَعَدَّى وَلِمَنِ الرِّبْحُ، نمبر 15121)

اصول: وکیل نے اپنی رقم موکل کے لئے لگائی ہے تو وکیل اپنی رقم لینے کا حق رکھتا ہے۔
Whoever appoints a man to buy something for him, it is necessary to specify its genus and description, or its genus and price, unless he appoints him with a general agency, saying: 'Buy for me whatever you see.' When the agent purchases and receives the sold item, then discovers a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect as long as the item is in his hand. If he delivers it to the principal, he cannot return it except with his permission. Agency is valid for currency exchange and salam contracts. If the agent separates from his counterpart before taking possession, the contract is void, and the separation of the principal is not considered. If the agent pays the price from his own money and receives the sold item, he has the right to recover it from the principal. If the sold item is destroyed in his hand before he detains it, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the price is not dropped. He has the right to detain it until he recovers the price. If he detains it and it is destroyed in his hand, it is guaranteed like a pledge according to Abu Yusuf, and like a sold item according to Muhammad. If a man appoints two men, neither may act alone in what they were appointed for, unless they are appointed for litigation, divorce of his wife without compensation, freeing his slave without compensation, returning a deposit, a loan, a usurped item, or paying a debt. [Then hadith evidence and usul notes.]
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This is a ruling passage with proofs from Al-Quduri. The text specifies the requirements for a valid purchase agency: the principal must specify the genus and description or genus and price of the item to be bought, unless he gives a general agency (e.g., 'buy whatever you see'). The agent has the right to return defective goods as long as they remain in his possession; after delivery to the principal, he needs permission. Agency for currency exchange (sarf) and salam is valid; if the agent separates from the counterparty before taking possession, the contract becomes void, but the principal's separation is irrelevant. If the agent uses his own funds, he can recover the price from the principal. If the goods are destroyed before the agent detains them (i.e., before exercising his right to withhold them for reimbursement), the loss is the principal's. But if the agent detains them and they are destroyed, there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf (who likens it to a pledge, so the agent is liable like a pledgee) and Muhammad (who likens it to a sold item, so the agent is liable as if he bought it). For joint agency, both agents must act together except in specified cases where acting alone is allowed: litigation, divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning deposits or loans, returning usurped items, or paying debts. Hadith proofs are provided for the validity of agency in sarf (from Umar and Ibn Umar) and for the rule of destruction before detention (from Abu Hurayrah regarding zakat, and from Hasan al-Basri about the mudarib being a trustee). The usul note reiterates that when an agent uses his own money, he has a right to reimbursement.

Key Terms
وكالة عامة (wakālah ʿāmmah): General agency where the principal says 'buy whatever you see', not specifying the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when may an agent return defective goods without the principal's permission?
A) Only if the principal explicitly allowed returns
B) Only if the agent paid from his own money
C) As long as the goods are still in the agent's hand
D) Only before the agent takes possession

Key Takeaway
A purchase agent must receive clear instructions on what to buy, and retains the right to return defective goods only while they are in his possession.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Liability for Goods Destroyed in Agent's Hands
Detailed ruling on destruction of goods and detention by agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of liability when goods purchased by an agent are destroyed, distinguishing between destruction before and after detention, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the nature of the agent's liability after detention.

Core Idea
Goods destroyed before the agent detains them are the principal's loss; after detention, the agent's liability is disputed — pledge-like or sale-like.

This section of Al-Quduri addresses a critical scenario: when the agent uses his own money to buy goods for the principal, what happens if the goods are destroyed? The text distinguishes two situations: destruction before the agent detains (withholds) the goods for reimbursement, and destruction after detention. In the first case, the loss falls on the principal. In the second case, the agent becomes liable, but the precise nature of that liability is disputed between the two great disciples — Abu Yusuf likens it to a pledge (daman al-rahn), while Muhammad likens it to a sold item (daman al-mabi'). The hadith of Abu Hurayrah is cited to support the rule for destruction before detention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent's right when using his own funds
Read the text that says if the agent pays from his own money and receives goods, he may recover the price from the principal. This establishes that the agent is not making a gift; he is entitled to reimbursement.
Text: 'فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ'.
2
Understand destruction before detention
If the goods are destroyed while in the agent's hand but before he detains them (i.e., before he exercises his right to withhold them as security for reimbursement), the loss is from the principal's wealth. The agent is not liable, and the principal still owes the price.
Text: 'فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُوَكِّلِ وَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ الثَّمَنُ'.
3
Recognize the agent's right to detain the goods
The agent has the right to withhold the goods until the principal pays him back. This is a security measure (habs).
Text: 'وَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ'.
4
Analyze the dispute after detention
If the agent detains the goods and they are destroyed, the liability is now on the agent. But what kind of liability? Abu Yusuf says it is like a pledge (daman al-rahn) — the agent is liable as a pledgee. Muhammad says it is like the sold item (daman al-mabi') — the agent is liable as if he bought it, meaning he must pay the full price.
Text: 'فَإِنْ حَبَسَهُ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ كَانَ مَضْمُونًا ضَمَانَ الرَّهْنِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَضَمَانَ الْمَبِيعِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ'.
5
Evaluate the practical difference
Under Abu Yusuf's view, if the goods are destroyed, the agent's liability is limited to the value of the goods (which is the amount he can recover from the principal? Actually, for pledge, if pledge is destroyed, the pledgee's right to the debt is reduced. For sale, if the buyer destroys the goods, he still owes the price. So the practical difference is whether the agent's right to reimbursement is reduced (Abu Yusuf) or not (Muhammad).
Further study may clarify; but the text does not give the outcome. The lesson is to recognize the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا لِيَشْتَرِيَ لَهُ شَيْئًا فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَسْمِيَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَصِفَتِهِ أَوْ جِنْسِهِ وَمَبْلَعِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُ وَكَالَةً عَامَّةً فَيَقُولَ لَهُ ابْتَعْ لِي مَا رَأَيْت

فَإِذَا اشْتَرَى الْوَكِيلُ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ ثُمَّ اطَّلَعَ عَلَى عَيْبٍ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ بِالْعَيْبِ مَا دَامَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ

وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَمِ فَإِنْ فَارَقَ الْوَكِيلُ صَاحِبَهُ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ وَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ مُفَارَقَةُ الْمُوَكِّلِ

وَإِذَا دَفَعَ الْوَكِيلُ بِالشِّرَاءِ الثَّمَنَ مِنْ مَالِهِ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ

فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُوَكِّلِ وَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ الثَّمَنُ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ فَإِنْ حَبَسَهُ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ كَانَ مَضْمُونًا ضَمَانَ الرَّهْنِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَضَمَانَ الْمَبِيعِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ

وَإِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ رَجُلَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيمَا وُكِّلَا فِيهِ دُونَ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُمَا بِالْخُصُومَةِ أَوْ بِطَلَاقِ زَوْجَتِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِعِتْقِ عَبْدِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِرَدِّ وَدِيعَةٍ أَوْ عَارِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَصْبٍ أَوْ بِقَضَاءِ دَيْنٍ

قَالَ: «كُنتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَفَرٍ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمْنَا الْمَدِينَةَ، قَالَ: يَا بِلَالُ، اقْضِهِ وَزِدْهُ، فَأَعْطَاهُ أَرْبَعَةَ دَنَانِيرَ وَزَادَهُ قِيرَاطًا، بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ أَنْ يُعْطِيَ شَيْئًا وَلَمْ يبين، غبر، 2309)

وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَم: وَقَدْ وَكَّلَ عُمَرُ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ فِي الصَّرْفِ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْوَكَالَةِ فِي الصَّرْفِ وَالْمِيزَانِ، نمبر 2302)

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ «وَكَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِحِفْظِ زَكَاةِ رَمَضَانَ فَأَتَانِي آتٍ فَجَعَلَ يَحْنُو مِنَ الطَّعَامِ فَأَخَذْتُهُ وَقُلْتُ وَاللَّهِ لأَرْفَعَنَّكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِنِّي مُحْتَاجٌ وَعَلَيَّ عِيَالٌ وَلِي حَاجَةٌ شَدِيدَةٌ قَالَ فَخَلَّيْتُ عَنْهُ،، (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا فَتَرَكَ الْوَكِيلُ شَيْئًا فَأَجَازَهُ الْمُوَكَّلُ، نمبر، 2311)

وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: الْمُضَارِبُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، وَإِنْ تَعَدَّى أَمْرَكَ، » مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ: ضَمَانُ الْمُقَارَضِ إِذَا تَعَدَّى وَلِمَنِ الرِّبْحُ، نمبر 15121)

اصول: وکیل نے اپنی رقم موکل کے لئے لگائی ہے تو وکیل اپنی رقم لینے کا حق رکھتا ہے۔
Whoever appoints a man to buy something for him, it is necessary to specify its genus and description, or its genus and price, unless he appoints him with a general agency, saying: 'Buy for me whatever you see.' When the agent purchases and receives the sold item, then discovers a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect as long as the item is in his hand. If he delivers it to the principal, he cannot return it except with his permission. Agency is valid for currency exchange and salam contracts. If the agent separates from his counterpart before taking possession, the contract is void, and the separation of the principal is not considered. If the agent pays the price from his own money and receives the sold item, he has the right to recover it from the principal. If the sold item is destroyed in his hand before he detains it, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the price is not dropped. He has the right to detain it until he recovers the price. If he detains it and it is destroyed in his hand, it is guaranteed like a pledge according to Abu Yusuf, and like a sold item according to Muhammad. If a man appoints two men, neither may act alone in what they were appointed for, unless they are appointed for litigation, divorce of his wife without compensation, freeing his slave without compensation, returning a deposit, a loan, a usurped item, or paying a debt. [Then hadith evidence and usul notes.]
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This is a ruling passage with proofs from Al-Quduri. The text specifies the requirements for a valid purchase agency: the principal must specify the genus and description or genus and price of the item to be bought, unless he gives a general agency (e.g., 'buy whatever you see'). The agent has the right to return defective goods as long as they remain in his possession; after delivery to the principal, he needs permission. Agency for currency exchange (sarf) and salam is valid; if the agent separates from the counterparty before taking possession, the contract becomes void, but the principal's separation is irrelevant. If the agent uses his own funds, he can recover the price from the principal. If the goods are destroyed before the agent detains them (i.e., before exercising his right to withhold them for reimbursement), the loss is the principal's. But if the agent detains them and they are destroyed, there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf (who likens it to a pledge, so the agent is liable like a pledgee) and Muhammad (who likens it to a sold item, so the agent is liable as if he bought it). For joint agency, both agents must act together except in specified cases where acting alone is allowed: litigation, divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning deposits or loans, returning usurped items, or paying debts. Hadith proofs are provided for the validity of agency in sarf (from Umar and Ibn Umar) and for the rule of destruction before detention (from Abu Hurayrah regarding zakat, and from Hasan al-Basri about the mudarib being a trustee). The usul note reiterates that when an agent uses his own money, he has a right to reimbursement.

Key Terms
ضمان الرهن (ḍamān al-rahn): Liability of a pledgee; the agent becomes liable for the goods as if he were holding a pledge.
ضمان المبيع (ḍamān al-mabīʿ): Liability of a sold item; the agent becomes liable as a buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the goods are destroyed after the agent detains them, the liability is:
A) Always the principal's
B) Always the agent's, but the nature is disputed
C) The seller's, since the agent detained them
D) The agent's only if he was negligent

Key Takeaway
The agent's liability for destroyed goods hinges on detention: before detention, the principal bears the loss; after detention, the agent bears it, with a school-internal dispute on the form of liability.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Special Contracts and Joint Agency
Rulings on agency in sarf/salam and on joint agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that agency is valid for currency exchange (ṣarf) and forward sale (salam), identify the condition of immediate possession and the consequence of separation before possession, list the general rule for joint agents (must act together) and enumerate the exceptions where a single joint agent may act alone.

Core Idea
Agency for sarf and salam is valid but requires immediate separation; joint agents must act together except in specific, limited actions.

This part of Al-Quduri addresses two separate topics: the validity of agency in specific contracts (currency exchange and forward sale) and the rules of joint agency. For sarf and salam, the agent can act, but if he separates from the other party before taking possession, the contract becomes void — and interestingly, the separation of the principal does not affect it. For joint agency, the general rule is that both agents must act together, but the text lists several exceptions where one agent may act alone, such as litigation, divorce without compensation, and returning deposits. These rules prevent deadlock and allow practical flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Understand agency in sarf and salam
Read the sentence that validates agency for these two contracts. Note that the agent can be the buyer or seller.
Text: 'وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَمِ'.
2
Identify the condition for validity in these contracts
In sarf and salam, possession must be immediate. If the agent separates from the other party before taking possession, the contract is void. The separation of the principal is irrelevant.
Text: 'فَإِنْ فَارَقَ الْوَكِيلُ صَاحِبَهُ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ وَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ مُفَارَقَةُ الْمُوَكِّلِ'.
3
Learn the general rule for joint agency
When two agents are appointed, neither can act alone in the matter they were appointed for. They must act jointly.
Text: 'وَإِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ رَجُلَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيمَا وُكِّلَا فِيهِ دُونَ الْآخَرِ'.
4
Memorize the exceptions for joint agency
The text lists situations where a single joint agent may act alone: litigation, divorce without compensation, freeing a slave without compensation, returning a deposit, a loan, a usurped item, or paying a debt.
Text: 'إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُمَا بِالْخُصُومَةِ أَوْ بِطَلَاقِ زَوْجَتِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِعِتْقِ عَبْدِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِرَدِّ وَدِيعَةٍ أَوْ عَارِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَصْبٍ أَوْ بِقَضَاءِ دَيْنٍ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا لِيَشْتَرِيَ لَهُ شَيْئًا فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَسْمِيَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَصِفَتِهِ أَوْ جِنْسِهِ وَمَبْلَعِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُ وَكَالَةً عَامَّةً فَيَقُولَ لَهُ ابْتَعْ لِي مَا رَأَيْت

فَإِذَا اشْتَرَى الْوَكِيلُ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ ثُمَّ اطَّلَعَ عَلَى عَيْبٍ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ بِالْعَيْبِ مَا دَامَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ

وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَمِ فَإِنْ فَارَقَ الْوَكِيلُ صَاحِبَهُ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ وَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ مُفَارَقَةُ الْمُوَكِّلِ

وَإِذَا دَفَعَ الْوَكِيلُ بِالشِّرَاءِ الثَّمَنَ مِنْ مَالِهِ وَقَبَضَ الْمَبِيعَ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ عَلَى الْمُوَكِّلِ

فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ هَلَكَ مِنْ مَالِ الْمُوَكِّلِ وَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ الثَّمَنُ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْبِسَهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ فَإِنْ حَبَسَهُ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ كَانَ مَضْمُونًا ضَمَانَ الرَّهْنِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَضَمَانَ الْمَبِيعِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ

وَإِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ رَجُلَيْنِ فَلَيْسَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيمَا وُكِّلَا فِيهِ دُونَ الْآخَرِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَكَّلَهُمَا بِالْخُصُومَةِ أَوْ بِطَلَاقِ زَوْجَتِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِعِتْقِ عَبْدِهِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ بِرَدِّ وَدِيعَةٍ أَوْ عَارِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَصْبٍ أَوْ بِقَضَاءِ دَيْنٍ

قَالَ: «كُنتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي سَفَرٍ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمْنَا الْمَدِينَةَ، قَالَ: يَا بِلَالُ، اقْضِهِ وَزِدْهُ، فَأَعْطَاهُ أَرْبَعَةَ دَنَانِيرَ وَزَادَهُ قِيرَاطًا، بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلٌ أَنْ يُعْطِيَ شَيْئًا وَلَمْ يبين، غبر، 2309)

وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّوْكِيلُ بِعَقْدِ الصَّرْفِ وَالسَّلَم: وَقَدْ وَكَّلَ عُمَرُ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ فِي الصَّرْفِ ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الْوَكَالَةِ فِي الصَّرْفِ وَالْمِيزَانِ، نمبر 2302)

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ «وَكَّلَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِحِفْظِ زَكَاةِ رَمَضَانَ فَأَتَانِي آتٍ فَجَعَلَ يَحْنُو مِنَ الطَّعَامِ فَأَخَذْتُهُ وَقُلْتُ وَاللَّهِ لأَرْفَعَنَّكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِنِّي مُحْتَاجٌ وَعَلَيَّ عِيَالٌ وَلِي حَاجَةٌ شَدِيدَةٌ قَالَ فَخَلَّيْتُ عَنْهُ،، (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : إِذَا وَكَّلَ رَجُلًا فَتَرَكَ الْوَكِيلُ شَيْئًا فَأَجَازَهُ الْمُوَكَّلُ، نمبر، 2311)

وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَبِيعُ فِي يَدِهِ قَبْلَ حَبْسِهِ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: الْمُضَارِبُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، وَإِنْ تَعَدَّى أَمْرَكَ، » مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ: ضَمَانُ الْمُقَارَضِ إِذَا تَعَدَّى وَلِمَنِ الرِّبْحُ، نمبر 15121)

اصول: وکیل نے اپنی رقم موکل کے لئے لگائی ہے تو وکیل اپنی رقم لینے کا حق رکھتا ہے۔
Whoever appoints a man to buy something for him, it is necessary to specify its genus and description, or its genus and price, unless he appoints him with a general agency, saying: 'Buy for me whatever you see.' When the agent purchases and receives the sold item, then discovers a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect as long as the item is in his hand. If he delivers it to the principal, he cannot return it except with his permission. Agency is valid for currency exchange and salam contracts. If the agent separates from his counterpart before taking possession, the contract is void, and the separation of the principal is not considered. If the agent pays the price from his own money and receives the sold item, he has the right to recover it from the principal. If the sold item is destroyed in his hand before he detains it, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the price is not dropped. He has the right to detain it until he recovers the price. If he detains it and it is destroyed in his hand, it is guaranteed like a pledge according to Abu Yusuf, and like a sold item according to Muhammad. If a man appoints two men, neither may act alone in what they were appointed for, unless they are appointed for litigation, divorce of his wife without compensation, freeing his slave without compensation, returning a deposit, a loan, a usurped item, or paying a debt. [Then hadith evidence and usul notes.]
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This is a ruling passage with proofs from Al-Quduri. The text specifies the requirements for a valid purchase agency: the principal must specify the genus and description or genus and price of the item to be bought, unless he gives a general agency (e.g., 'buy whatever you see'). The agent has the right to return defective goods as long as they remain in his possession; after delivery to the principal, he needs permission. Agency for currency exchange (sarf) and salam is valid; if the agent separates from the counterparty before taking possession, the contract becomes void, but the principal's separation is irrelevant. If the agent uses his own funds, he can recover the price from the principal. If the goods are destroyed before the agent detains them (i.e., before exercising his right to withhold them for reimbursement), the loss is the principal's. But if the agent detains them and they are destroyed, there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf (who likens it to a pledge, so the agent is liable like a pledgee) and Muhammad (who likens it to a sold item, so the agent is liable as if he bought it). For joint agency, both agents must act together except in specified cases where acting alone is allowed: litigation, divorce without compensation, manumission without compensation, returning deposits or loans, returning usurped items, or paying debts. Hadith proofs are provided for the validity of agency in sarf (from Umar and Ibn Umar) and for the rule of destruction before detention (from Abu Hurayrah regarding zakat, and from Hasan al-Basri about the mudarib being a trustee). The usul note reiterates that when an agent uses his own money, he has a right to reimbursement.

Key Terms
صرف (ṣarf): Currency exchange (sale of gold for silver, etc.), which requires hand-to-hand possession.
سلم (salam): Forward sale (advance payment for future delivery) where the price is paid immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is an exception where a joint agent may act alone?
A) Selling a house
B) Paying a debt
C) Buying a car
D) Hiring a worker

Key Takeaway
Agency in sarf and salam requires immediate possession; joint agents must act together except in specifically enumerated, non‑financial actions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Agent Exceeding Instructions: The Binding Effect of Extra Quantity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's excess purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on whether an agent's purchase of excess quantity binds the principal, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
An agent who exceeds numeric instructions does not bind the principal for the excess, even if beneficial.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when an agent buys more than instructed but at a bargain price? The principal told the agent to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham; the agent finds a deal and buys 20 ratls for 1 dirham. The meat normally sells at 10 ratls per dirham, so the agent got double the quantity for the same price. Did the principal benefit or did the agent overstep? The great imams differed, and we will examine why their difference matters in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Core Issue
Read the Arabic passage carefully: the principal instructed the agent to buy 10 ratls for 1 dirham. The agent bought 20 ratls for 1 dirham, at a time when 10 ratls normally cost 1 dirham. So the agent effectively paid 1 dirham for 20 ratls, a 50% discount. The question: is the principal bound to accept all 20 ratls (paying only 1 dirham) or only 10 ratls (paying 0.5 dirham)?
The market price is crucial: 10 ratls = 1 dirham. So 20 ratls normally cost 2 dirhams. The agent paid only 1 dirham, a clear benefit.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa holds that only 10 ratls bind the principal at half the price (0.5 dirham). The remaining 10 ratls are the agent's own purchase. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that all 20 ratls bind the principal at 1 dirham.
Note: both sides agree the purchase is valid; the dispute is over who bears the excess and at what price.
3
Examine the Proofs for Each Position
The Sahibayn rely on a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ gave Urwa a dinar to buy a sacrificial animal; Urwa bought two and sold one, returning a sheep and a dinar. The Prophet praised him, showing that exceeding instructions for benefit is approved. Abu Hanifa counters that the numeric limit here is explicit; the hadith involved discretion, not a fixed count.
The hadith is cited as a proof for permissibility, but Abu Hanifa restricts its application to cases where the agent has no explicit numeric limit.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Why
Later Hanafi authorities, such as Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah, prefer Abu Hanifa's view as more cautious and consistent with the principle that the agent cannot impose an unconsented transaction on the principal. Thus the operative fatwa is: the principal is bound only for 10 ratls at half price.
This is an example of tarjih within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَكَلَهُ بِشِرَاءِ عَشَرَةِ أَرْطَالِ لَحْمٍ بِدِرْهَمٍ فَاشْتَرَى عِشْرِينَ رِطْلًا بِدِرْهَمٍ مِنْ لَحْمٍ يُبَاعُ مِثْلُهُ عَشَرَةُ أَرْطَالٍ بِدِرْهَمٍ لَزِمَ الْمُوَكَّلَ مِنْهُ عَشَرَةٌ بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَلْزَمُهُ الْعِشْرُونَ
And if he authorized him to purchase ten ratls of meat for a dirham, and he bought twenty ratls for a dirham of meat whose like sells at ten ratls for a dirham, then upon the principal are binding from it ten (ratls) for half a dirham according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the twenty are binding upon him.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning an agent who exceeds the principal's instruction. The principal instructed the agent to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham. The agent instead buys 20 ratls of the same quality for 1 dirham (which normally costs 2 dirhams at the market rate). Since the agent paid only 1 dirham, he effectively got a bargain. Abu Hanifa rules that only 10 ratls bind the principal at half the price (0.5 dirham), because the instruction was clear and the agent exceeded it. The remaining 10 ratls are the agent's own transaction. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) rule that the entire 20 ratls bind the principal because the agent acted for the principal's benefit and the market rate makes the purchase favorable. The principal gets the entire 20 at a favorable price. The proof cited is the hadith of Urwa ibn Abi al-Ja'd al-Bariqi where the Prophet ﷺ gave him a dinar to buy a sacrificial animal, and he bought two and sold one, returning a sheep and a dinar. This shows permissibility of exceeding instructions for benefit. However, the madhhab's position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa in this case, as per later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
وَكِيلٌ (wakīl): An agent authorized to act on behalf of another (principal) in a specific transaction.
يَتَغَابَنُ النَّاسُ فِي مِثْلِهَا (yataghābanu al-nāsu fī mithlihā): A degree of overpayment that people customarily tolerate in similar transactions (ghabn yasīr).
لَزِمَ (lazima): The purchase becomes binding upon the principal; he is obligated to accept and pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the key factor that determines whether the principal is bound for the extra 10 ratls under Abu Hanifa's view?
A) The agent's good intention to benefit the principal.
B) The fact that the instruction was a numeric limit.
C) The market price being the same as the instruction price.
D) The agent's personal connection to the seller.

Key Takeaway
An agent who exceeds a numeric instruction does not bind the principal for the excess, even if it is a bargain, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The Dislike of Suftaja: Loan with Benefit as Usury
Ruling that suftaja is makruh with supporting proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suftaja, explain why it is makruh, and apply the principle that any loan bringing benefit is a form of riba.

Core Idea
Any loan that gives the lender a benefit resembles usury and is disliked.

Suftaja, a bill of exchange where the lender avoids travel risk, is ruled makruh in the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs from the Qur'anic principle, hadith, and companion practice. You will learn how even non-monetary benefits can taint a loan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its classification
Read the first sentence: the author states suftaja is disliked (makruh). Determine the precise hukm level: it is makruh tanzihan not haram, because the benefit is incidental, not stipulated.
The term 'makruh' here implies tanzih (disliked, not prohibited).
2
Understand the rationale
The author explains: the lender gains safety from road danger (amna khatar al-tariq). This is a benefit derived from the loan, which triggers the principle: every loan that brings a benefit is a form of riba.
The benefit here is not an increase in the principal but an avoidance of risk.
3
Analyze the proofs
Three proofs: (1) Hadith of Zaynab advising against delivery without guarantee; (2) Statement of Fadalah ibn Ubayd: any loan with benefit is riba; (3) Practice of Ibn al-Zubayr and Ibn Abbas's approval only if exactly by weight. Identify how each proof supports the ruling.
Focus on the common theme: avoiding any extra benefit in a loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ السَّفَاتِجُ وَهُوَ قَرْضٌ اسْتَفَادَ بِهِ الْمُقْرِضُ أَمْنَ خَطَرِ الطَّرِيقِ. عَنْ زَيْنَبَ، قَالَتْ: أَعْطَانِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ خَمْسِينَ وَسْقًا تَمَرًا بِخَيْبَرَ وَعِشْرِينَ شَعِيرًا، قَالَتْ: فَجَاءَنِي عَاصِمُ بْنُ عَدِي، فَقَالَ لِي: هَلْ لَكِ أَنْ أُوتِيَكِ مَالَكِ بِخَيْبَرَ هَا هُنَا بِالْمَدِينَةِ فَأَقْبَضَهُ مِنْكِ بِكَيْلِهِ بِخَيْبَرَ؟ فَقَالَتْ: لَا حَتَّى أَسْأَلَ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، قَالَتْ: فَذَكَرْتُ ذَلِكَ لِعُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ، فَقَالَ: لَا تَفْعَلِي فَكَيْفَ لَكِ بِالضَّمَانِ فِيمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ. عَنْ فَضَالَةَ بْنِ عُبَيْدٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: كُلُّ قَرْضٍ جَرَّ مَنْفَعَةً فَهُوَ وَجْهٌ مِنْ وُجُوهِ الرِّبَا. وَأَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ الزُّبَيْرِ كَانَ يَأْخُذُ مِنْ قَوْمٍ بِمَكَّةَ دَرَاهِمَ، ثُمَّ يَكْتُبُ بِمَا إِلَى مُصْعَبِ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ بِالْعِرَاقِ فَيَأْخُذُونَهَا مِنْهُ، فَسُئِلَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَلَمْ يَرَ بِهِ بَأْسًا، فَقِيلَ لَهُ: إِنْ أَخَذُوا أَفْضَلَ مِنْ دَرَاهِمِهِمْ، قَالَ: لَا بَأْسَ إِذَا أَخَذُوا بِوَزْنِ دَرَاهِمِهِمْ.
And the suftaja is disliked, which is a loan by which the lender gains safety from the danger of the road. From Zaynab: she said, 'The Messenger of Allah gave me fifty wasqs of dates in Khaybar and twenty of barley.' She said, 'Asim ibn Adi came to me and said, 'Would you like me to bring your property from Khaybar here to Medina and I will give it to you by its measure in Khaybar?' She said, 'No, until I ask about that.' She said, 'I mentioned that to Umar ibn al-Khattab, and he said, 'Do not do it, for how will you guarantee what is between that?'' From Fadalah ibn Ubayd that he said: 'Every loan that brings a benefit is a form of usury.' And that Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr used to take dirhams from people in Makkah, then write for them to Mus'ab ibn al-Zubayr in Iraq, and they would take it from him. Ibn Abbas was asked about that and he saw no harm in it. It was said to him: 'If they take better than their dirhams?' He said: 'No harm if they take by the weight of their dirhams.'
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that suftaja (a bill of exchange or a loan where the lender provides money in one location to be repaid in another, thereby avoiding the risk of travel) is makruh (disliked). The reason is that the lender gains a benefit (safety from travel risk) from the loan, which constitutes a form of usury. The text provides three proofs: (1) The hadith of Zaynab: she was offered to have her dates from Khaybar delivered in Medina, equivalent in measure, but Umar ibn al-Khattab advised against it due to the uncertainty of guarantee. This shows that any loan or credit that involves a benefit to the lender (here, delivery without risk) is problematic. (2) The statement of Fadalah ibn Ubayd (a companion) that any loan that brings a benefit is a form of usury, which is a general principle. (3) The practice of Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr and Ibn Abbas's approval: Ibn al-Zubayr would give money in Makkah and have it paid in Iraq, but Ibn Abbas allowed it only if the payment was by weight (i.e., exact same amount). The Hanafi position is that suftaja is makruh tanzihan (disliked, not prohibited) because the benefit is not a clear increase in the loan amount but a security benefit. The Urdu principles mention that every loan that brings benefit is a type of usury; here the benefit is safety from road danger.

Key Terms
سَفَاتِج (suftaja): A bill of exchange or a loan where the lender provides money in one place to be repaid in another, securing safety from travel risk
قَرْض (qard): Loan
رِبَا (riba): Usury or interest

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is suftaja considered makruh in the Hanafi school?
A) Because it involves a guaranteed profit
B) Because the lender gains safety from travel risk, which is a benefit from the loan
C) Because it is a form of gambling
D) Because it delays payment

Key Takeaway
Suftaja is makruh in the Hanafi school because any loan that gives the lender a benefit (even non-monetary) resembles riba.
