Types of Sulh and Their Legal Nature
Defines three types of sulh and their legal nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of sulh (with acknowledgment, silence, and denial) and classify each as either a sale or lease contract according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sulh is valid in all three forms; its legal effect depends on the defendant's stance and the subject matter.

In this lesson, we examine the opening of al-Quduri's Book of Sulh. The author defines three categories of settlement based on how the defendant responds to the claim: acknowledgment, silence, or denial. Understanding this classification is essential because it determines whether the settlement is treated as a sale, a lease, or a mere compromise to end litigation. We will also see the underlying proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish the general permissibility of sulh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of sulh
Read the first sentence of the passage: 'Sulh is of three types: sulh with acknowledgment, sulh with silence, and sulh with denial.' Note that each type is defined by the defendant's response to the claim.
The Hanafi school considers all three valid, while some other schools reject sulh with denial.
2
Classify the legal nature of each type
For sulh with acknowledgment, the author says it is treated like a sale if it involves property-for-property, and like a lease if it involves property-for-benefits. For sulh with silence or denial, it is treated as a commutative contract for the plaintiff and as a ransom from oath for the defendant.
This distinction affects the rights and obligations of the parties, e.g., warranty, defects, and preemption.
3
Extract the ruling on validity
The text explicitly states 'All of that is permissible' (kullu dhālika jā'iz). This is the operative ruling: all three forms are valid in Hanafi fiqh.
The hadith 'al-sulhu jā'iz bayna al-muslimīn' is the primary proof.
4
Apply the classification to a scenario
Consider a dispute over a house: if the defendant acknowledges the claim and settles by giving a different property, it follows sale rules (e.g., option of inspection). If the defendant remains silent, it follows the rules of compromise for oath-avoidance.
Practice applying the rules to real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصُّلح
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى - الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبٍ صُلْحٌ مَعَ إِقْرَارٍ وَصُلْحٌ مَعَ سُكُوتٍ وَهُوَ أَنْ لَا يُقرَّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُنْكِرُ وَصُلْحٌ مَعَ إِنْكَارٍ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ جَائِزٌ
ل فَإِنْ وَقَعَ الصُّلْحُ عَلَى الْإِقْرَارِ اعْتُبِرَ فِيهِ مَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْبَيَاعَاتِ إِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ مَالٍ بِمَالٍ وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ مَالِ بِمَنَافِعَ اعْتُبِرَ بِالْإِجَارَاتِ وَالصُّلْحُ عَنْ السُّكُوتِ وَالْإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِافْتِدَاءِ الْيَمِينِ وَقَطْعِ الْخُصُومَةِ وَفِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعِي بِمَعْنَى الْمُعَاوَضَةِ
وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَنْ دَارٍ لَمْ تَجِبْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَارٍ وَجَبَتْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصَّلْحُ عَنْ إِقْرَارٍ فَاسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الْمُصَالَحِ عَنْهُ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِحِصَّةِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ الْعِوَضِ
وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ سُكُوتٍ أَوْ إِنْكَارِ فَاسْتَحِقَّ الْمُتَنَازَعُ فِيهِ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعِي بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَرَدَّ الْعِوَضَ وَإِنْ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ ذَلِكَ رَدَّ حِصَّتَهُ وَرَجَعَ بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَإِنْ ادَّعَى حَقًّا فِي دَارِ لَمْ يُبَيِّنْهُ فَصُولِحَ عَنْهُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ ثُمَّ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ الدَّارِ لَمْ يَرُدُّ شَيْئًا مِنْ الْعِوَضِ
لوجه: (1) الآية الثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ ا ﴿وَإِنِ امْرَأَةٌ خَافَتْ مِنْ بَعْلِهَا نُشُورًا أَوْ إِعْرَاضًا فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا أَن يُصْلِحَا بَيْنَهُمَا صُلْحَا وَالصُّلْحُ خَيْرٌ﴾ (سورة النساء، 128)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: صَالَحَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمُشْرِكِينَ يَوْمَ الْحَدَيْبِيَةِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَشْيَاءَ عَلَى أَنَّ مَنْ أَتَاهُ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ رَدَّهُ إِلَيْهِمْ وَمَنْ أَتَاهُمْ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ لَمْ يَرُدُّوهُ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الصُّلْح مَعَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، برقم 2700)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : الصُّلْحُ جَائِزٌ بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ» زَادَ أَحْمَدُ، «إِلَّا صُلْحًا أَحَلَّ حَرَامًا، أَوْ حَرَّمَ حَلَالًا» (سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابٌ فِي الصُّلْحِ، نمبر 3594)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالصُّلْحُ عَنْ السُّكُوتِ وَالإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعَى عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ مَظْلِمَةٌ لِأَحَدٍ مِنْ عِرْضِهِ أَوْ شَيْءٍ فَلْيَتَحَلَّلْهُ مِنْهُ الْيَوْمَ، قَبْلَ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ دِينَارٌ وَلَا دِرْهَمْ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ مَظْلَمَةٌ عِنْدَ الرَّجُلِ فَحَلَّلَهَا لَهُ هَلْ يُبَيِّنُ مَظْلَمَتَهُ، غير 2449)
اصول شریعت میں ہر صلح جائز ہے، سوائے وہ جو حرام کو حلال کر دے یا حلال کو حرام کر دے۔
Book of Sulh. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - Sulh is of three types: sulh with acknowledgment, sulh with silence (i.e., the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies), and sulh with denial. All of that is permissible. If sulh occurs with acknowledgment, then what is considered in sales is considered if it is for property in exchange for property, and if it is for property in exchange for benefits, it is considered by the rules of leases. Sulh with silence and denial is, for the defendant, to ransom the oath and to cut off the litigation, and for the plaintiff, it is in the sense of a commutative contract. And if one makes sulh from a house, preemption is not established therein; and if one makes sulh upon a house, preemption is established. And if the sulh is with acknowledgment, and part of the subject matter is reclaimed, the defendant takes back that proportionate share of the consideration. And if it occurs with silence or denial, and the contested thing is reclaimed, the plaintiff returns to litigation and returns the consideration. And if part of that is reclaimed, he returns its share and returns to litigation. And if someone claims a right in a house without specifying it, and makes sulh about it for something, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return anything from the consideration. For proof (1) the verse: "And if a woman fears from her husband contempt or evasion, there is no sin upon them if they make a settlement between them, and settlement is best." (Surah an-Nisa, 128). For proof (2) the hadith establishing that sulh is of three types: from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) made peace with the polytheists on the day of al-Hudaybiyya on three things: that whoever from the polytheists came to him, he would return him to them, and whoever from the Muslims came to them, they would not return him. (Bukhari, Book of Peace with Polytheists, no. 2700). For proof (3) the hadith establishing that sulh is of three types: from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Sulh is permissible between Muslims." Ahmad added: "Except a sulh that makes lawful what is unlawful or unlawful what is lawful." (Abu Dawud, Book of Sulh, no. 3594). For proof (1) the hadith establishing that sulh with silence and denial is for the defendant: from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever has done an injustice to someone regarding his honor or anything else, should settle the matter with him today, before the day when there will be no dinar nor dirham." (Bukhari, Book of Seeking Clarification from Injustice, no. 2449). Principle: In Islamic law, every sulh is permissible except one that makes the unlawful lawful or the lawful unlawful.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn on the Book of Sulh, followed by textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The author first classifies sulh into three categories based on the defendant's stance: acknowledgment, silence, or denial. All are valid in hanafi law. The legal nature of a sulh depends on the underlying claim: if with acknowledgment and involving exchange of property, it follows sale rules; if benefits, it follows lease rules. Sulh with silence or denial is considered a compromise to avoid an oath and end dispute, but for the plaintiff it is a commutative contract. Next, rulings on shuf'ah (preemption) are given: if a person makes a settlement to relinquish a claim on a house (sulh 'an), no preemption right arises; but if he acquires a house via sulh (sulh 'ala), preemption does apply. Then follow istiḥqāq (reclamation) scenarios: if after a sulh with acknowledgment part of the property is reclaimed by a third party, the defendant recovers a proportionate share of the consideration. If the sulh was with silence or denial and the whole of the disputed property is reclaimed, the plaintiff resumes litigation and returns the consideration. If only part is reclaimed, he returns its share and continues litigation. Finally, if someone claims an unspecified right in a house and settles for a sum, then part of the house is reclaimed (e.g. by a co-owner), he does not refund any consideration because his claim was vague. The proofs cite Quran 4:128 encouraging marital settlement, the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah as a precedent for conditional sulh, the general hadith that sulh is permissible except what alters legal prohibitions, and the hadith urging settlement of injustices before the afterlife. The Urdu conclusion reiterates that all sulh is allowed as long as it does not violate divine law.

Key Terms
صُلْح (ṣulḥ): A contract to end a dispute by mutual agreement, often involving a compromise on claims.
إِقْرَار (iqrār): Acknowledgment by the defendant of the plaintiff's claim.
سُكُوت (sukūt): Defendant's silence: neither admitting nor denying the claim.
إِنْكَار (inkār): Defendant's denial of the plaintiff's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, what is the legal nature of a sulh with silence or denial from the plaintiff's perspective?
A) It is a gift
B) It is a commutative contract (muʿāwaḍah)
C) It is a lease
D) It is a sale

Key Takeaway
Sulh is valid in all three forms (with acknowledgment, silence, or denial) and its legal nature depends on the type and the parties' perspectives.

Shuf'ah and Istiḥqāq in Sulh
Rulings on shuf'ah and istiḥqāq after sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on preemption (shuf'ah) and property reclamation (istiḥqāq) in the context of a settlement contract, distinguishing between sulh 'an and sulh 'alā.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah applies when acquiring property via sulh, not when relinquishing a claim; reclaimed property triggers proportional refund or continued litigation.

Building on the types of sulh, this lesson focuses on two important ancillary rulings: preemption (shuf'ah) and reclamation (istiḥqāq). These rules determine whether a co-owner can step into a purchaser's shoes after a settlement, and what happens if a third party proves ownership of the settled property. The passage distinguishes between sulh 'an (relinquishing a claim on a property) and sulh 'alā (acquiring a property via settlement), and provides detailed scenarios for reclamation based on the type of sulh.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'sulh from' vs 'sulh upon'
Read the sentence: 'وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَنْ دَارٍ لَمْ تَجِبْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَارٍ وَجَبَتْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ'. Note that the preposition changes the ruling on preemption.
Ṣulḥ ʿan means the plaintiff gives up a claim on the house; no ownership transfer to him, so no shuf'ah. Ṣulḥ ʿalā means he acquires the house, so shuf'ah applies.
2
Analyze istiḥqāq with acknowledgment
If after a sulh with acknowledgment part of the property is reclaimed (proven to belong to a third party), the defendant takes back a proportionate share of the consideration.
The consideration is apportioned because the defendant paid for the whole, but part is taken away.
3
Analyze istiḥqāq with silence or denial
If the entire contested property is reclaimed, the plaintiff returns to litigation and returns the consideration. If only part is reclaimed, he returns its share and continues litigation.
Here the plaintiff is treated as the buyer who loses the property.
4
Handle unspecified claim scenario
If someone claims an unspecified right in a house and settles for a sum, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not refund anything because his claim was vague.
The consideration is not apportioned because the claim was not defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصُّلح
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى - الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبٍ صُلْحٌ مَعَ إِقْرَارٍ وَصُلْحٌ مَعَ سُكُوتٍ وَهُوَ أَنْ لَا يُقرَّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُنْكِرُ وَصُلْحٌ مَعَ إِنْكَارٍ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ جَائِزٌ
ل فَإِنْ وَقَعَ الصُّلْحُ عَلَى الْإِقْرَارِ اعْتُبِرَ فِيهِ مَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْبَيَاعَاتِ إِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ مَالٍ بِمَالٍ وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ مَالِ بِمَنَافِعَ اعْتُبِرَ بِالْإِجَارَاتِ وَالصُّلْحُ عَنْ السُّكُوتِ وَالْإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِافْتِدَاءِ الْيَمِينِ وَقَطْعِ الْخُصُومَةِ وَفِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعِي بِمَعْنَى الْمُعَاوَضَةِ
وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَنْ دَارٍ لَمْ تَجِبْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَارٍ وَجَبَتْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصَّلْحُ عَنْ إِقْرَارٍ فَاسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الْمُصَالَحِ عَنْهُ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِحِصَّةِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ الْعِوَضِ
وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ سُكُوتٍ أَوْ إِنْكَارِ فَاسْتَحِقَّ الْمُتَنَازَعُ فِيهِ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعِي بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَرَدَّ الْعِوَضَ وَإِنْ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ ذَلِكَ رَدَّ حِصَّتَهُ وَرَجَعَ بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَإِنْ ادَّعَى حَقًّا فِي دَارِ لَمْ يُبَيِّنْهُ فَصُولِحَ عَنْهُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ ثُمَّ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ الدَّارِ لَمْ يَرُدُّ شَيْئًا مِنْ الْعِوَضِ
لوجه: (1) الآية الثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ ا ﴿وَإِنِ امْرَأَةٌ خَافَتْ مِنْ بَعْلِهَا نُشُورًا أَوْ إِعْرَاضًا فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا أَن يُصْلِحَا بَيْنَهُمَا صُلْحَا وَالصُّلْحُ خَيْرٌ﴾ (سورة النساء، 128)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: صَالَحَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمُشْرِكِينَ يَوْمَ الْحَدَيْبِيَةِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَشْيَاءَ عَلَى أَنَّ مَنْ أَتَاهُ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ رَدَّهُ إِلَيْهِمْ وَمَنْ أَتَاهُمْ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ لَمْ يَرُدُّوهُ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الصُّلْح مَعَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، برقم 2700)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت الصُّلْحُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَضْرُبِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : الصُّلْحُ جَائِزٌ بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ» زَادَ أَحْمَدُ، «إِلَّا صُلْحًا أَحَلَّ حَرَامًا، أَوْ حَرَّمَ حَلَالًا» (سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابٌ فِي الصُّلْحِ، نمبر 3594)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالصُّلْحُ عَنْ السُّكُوتِ وَالإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعَى عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ مَظْلِمَةٌ لِأَحَدٍ مِنْ عِرْضِهِ أَوْ شَيْءٍ فَلْيَتَحَلَّلْهُ مِنْهُ الْيَوْمَ، قَبْلَ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ دِينَارٌ وَلَا دِرْهَمْ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ مَظْلَمَةٌ عِنْدَ الرَّجُلِ فَحَلَّلَهَا لَهُ هَلْ يُبَيِّنُ مَظْلَمَتَهُ، غير 2449)
اصول شریعت میں ہر صلح جائز ہے، سوائے وہ جو حرام کو حلال کر دے یا حلال کو حرام کر دے۔
Book of Sulh. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - Sulh is of three types: sulh with acknowledgment, sulh with silence (i.e., the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies), and sulh with denial. All of that is permissible. If sulh occurs with acknowledgment, then what is considered in sales is considered if it is for property in exchange for property, and if it is for property in exchange for benefits, it is considered by the rules of leases. Sulh with silence and denial is, for the defendant, to ransom the oath and to cut off the litigation, and for the plaintiff, it is in the sense of a commutative contract. And if one makes sulh from a house, preemption is not established therein; and if one makes sulh upon a house, preemption is established. And if the sulh is with acknowledgment, and part of the subject matter is reclaimed, the defendant takes back that proportionate share of the consideration. And if it occurs with silence or denial, and the contested thing is reclaimed, the plaintiff returns to litigation and returns the consideration. And if part of that is reclaimed, he returns its share and returns to litigation. And if someone claims a right in a house without specifying it, and makes sulh about it for something, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return anything from the consideration. For proof (1) the verse: "And if a woman fears from her husband contempt or evasion, there is no sin upon them if they make a settlement between them, and settlement is best." (Surah an-Nisa, 128). For proof (2) the hadith establishing that sulh is of three types: from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) made peace with the polytheists on the day of al-Hudaybiyya on three things: that whoever from the polytheists came to him, he would return him to them, and whoever from the Muslims came to them, they would not return him. (Bukhari, Book of Peace with Polytheists, no. 2700). For proof (3) the hadith establishing that sulh is of three types: from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Sulh is permissible between Muslims." Ahmad added: "Except a sulh that makes lawful what is unlawful or unlawful what is lawful." (Abu Dawud, Book of Sulh, no. 3594). For proof (1) the hadith establishing that sulh with silence and denial is for the defendant: from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever has done an injustice to someone regarding his honor or anything else, should settle the matter with him today, before the day when there will be no dinar nor dirham." (Bukhari, Book of Seeking Clarification from Injustice, no. 2449). Principle: In Islamic law, every sulh is permissible except one that makes the unlawful lawful or the lawful unlawful.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn on the Book of Sulh, followed by textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The author first classifies sulh into three categories based on the defendant's stance: acknowledgment, silence, or denial. All are valid in hanafi law. The legal nature of a sulh depends on the underlying claim: if with acknowledgment and involving exchange of property, it follows sale rules; if benefits, it follows lease rules. Sulh with silence or denial is considered a compromise to avoid an oath and end dispute, but for the plaintiff it is a commutative contract. Next, rulings on shuf'ah (preemption) are given: if a person makes a settlement to relinquish a claim on a house (sulh 'an), no preemption right arises; but if he acquires a house via sulh (sulh 'ala), preemption does apply. Then follow istiḥqāq (reclamation) scenarios: if after a sulh with acknowledgment part of the property is reclaimed by a third party, the defendant recovers a proportionate share of the consideration. If the sulh was with silence or denial and the whole of the disputed property is reclaimed, the plaintiff resumes litigation and returns the consideration. If only part is reclaimed, he returns its share and continues litigation. Finally, if someone claims an unspecified right in a house and settles for a sum, then part of the house is reclaimed (e.g. by a co-owner), he does not refund any consideration because his claim was vague. The proofs cite Quran 4:128 encouraging marital settlement, the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah as a precedent for conditional sulh, the general hadith that sulh is permissible except what alters legal prohibitions, and the hadith urging settlement of injustices before the afterlife. The Urdu conclusion reiterates that all sulh is allowed as long as it does not violate divine law.

Key Terms
شُفْعَة (shufʿa): Right of preemption for a co-owner in a property to buy out a new purchaser.
اسْتِحْقَاق (istiḥqāq): Reclamation of property from a possessor by a third party who proves superior right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh with denial, if the entire disputed property is reclaimed by a third party, what is the plaintiff required to do according to the passage?
A) Keep the consideration and drop the case
B) Return the consideration and resume litigation
C) Return the consideration and sue the third party
D) Do nothing; the sulh remains valid

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah applies only when sulh transfers ownership (ṣulḥ ʿalā); istiḥqāq rules vary by sulh type, with no refund for unspecified claims.

Sulh on Salam Contract Between Partners
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sulh in salam partnership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the validity of a partner settling his salam share for the principal, and identify the mufta bihi position within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad invalidate the sulh; Abu Yusuf validates it – an intra-Hanafi variance on the nature of cancelling a salam.

This passage presents a concise but important intra-Hanafi disagreement. When two partners jointly own a salam contract (forward purchase), and one partner seeks to 'settle' with the seller by taking back his advance payment in exchange for his right to the future goods, Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule the settlement invalid. However, Abu Yusuf permits it. Understanding this nuance requires familiarity with the rules of salam and the concept of sulh in partnership contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
Recognize that the passage involves a salam contract jointly owned by two partners, and one partner wishes to settle with the seller by getting his principal back in place of his share of the future goods.
The key elements: partners, salam contract, sulh on the principal.
2
Note the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to 'them' (عندهم, which refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani), this sulh is invalid (لم يجز). Memorize this as the primary position.
This is the majority view within the early Hanafi school.
3
Note the dissent of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the sulh is valid (يجوز الصلح). This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
Abu Yusuf's view is recorded but not the relied-upon position.
4
Consider the basis of the dispute
Although the passage does not give reasoning, understand that the dispute likely revolves around whether sulh here is a cancellation (faskh) of the salam, which has strict conditions, or a new independent contract.
Cancellation of a salam is generally not allowed except by mutual rescission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّلَمُ بَيْنَ شَرِيكَيْنِ فَصَاحَ أَحَدُهُمَا مِنْ نَصِيبِهِ عَلَى رَأْسِ الْمَالِ لَمْ يَجُزْ عِنْدَهُمَا. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَجُوزُ الصُّلْحُ
And when there is a salam contract between two partners, and one of them settles from his share on the capital (principal), it is not valid according to them (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: the sulh is valid.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sulh on a salam (forward sale) contract between two partners. In a salam contract, the buyer pays the price in advance for goods to be delivered later. If two partners jointly own such a salam contract (i.e., they are both buyers), and one partner settles with the seller to take back his portion of the principal in exchange for forfeiting his right to the goods, Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (as-Sahibayn, though here 'عندهم' likely refers to the two) say it is invalid. However, Abu Yusuf permits it. The basis of the dispute likely relates to whether this sulh is treated as a cancellation of the salam, which has specific rules. The text does not elaborate the reasoning, but the positions are recorded for the student to note.

Key Terms
سَلَم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later. It is a contract with specific conditions.
رَأْسُ الْمَال (ra's al-māl): The principal or capital paid in a salam contract. Here, settling on the principal means the partner recovers his advance payment in exchange for giving up his right to receive the goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is not valid.
C) It is valid only if the other partner agrees.
D) It is valid only if the goods have been delivered.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute on salam sulh, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold it invalid; Abu Yusuf permits it, but the relied-upon position is invalidity.

Rulings on Sulh with Mixed Assets and Debts in Inheritance
Conditions for valid sulh when estate has different species and debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sulh (compromise) when an estate contains different species of assets and debts, and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Sulh in inheritance is valid if the exchanged value accounts for all shares, but debt inclusion requires proper release.

Compromise (sulh) is a common way to resolve inheritance disputes. When the estate contains different types of assets like gold, silver, and debts, the Hanafi school sets specific conditions to ensure fairness. This lesson examines the key rulings from al-Quduri's text, supported by hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the asset types in the estate
Determine if the estate is homogenous (one type, e.g., all silver), mixed (e.g., gold and silver), or includes debts owed by others.
2
Determine validity of exchanging one species for another
If the estate is homogenous, exchanging for a different species (e.g., silver for gold) is valid. If mixed, the amount given must exceed the party's share of that species to account for other assets.
This ensures the settlement covers the entire share.
3
Apply the condition for mixed estates
Calculate the minimum amount: the sum of the party's share of the species given plus enough to cover his share of other species.
Excess represents his right from the rest of the inheritance.
4
Analyze the treatment of debts in sulh
If the debt is included and the heirs retain it, sulh is void. It is valid only if they stipulate that the settlor is released and the debt does not revert to him.
Debt transfer before receipt is not permissible.
5
Review the supporting evidence
Examine the hadith from Ibn Abbas (permissibility of partners separating with debt/asset) and the practice of al-Hasan and Jabir.
These establish the legal basis for the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَتِ التَّرَكَةُ فِضَّةً فَأَعْطَوْهُ ذَهَبًا أَوْ ذَهَبًا فَأَعْطَوْهُ فِضَّةً فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ وَإِنْ كَانَتِ الشَّرِكَةُ ذَهَبًا وَفِضَّةً وَغَيْرَ ذَلِكَ فَصَالَحُوهُ عَلَى فِضَّةٍ أَوْ ذَهَبٍ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَا أَعْطَوْهُ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ نَصِيبِهِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ الْجِنْسِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ نَصِيبُهُ مِثْلَهُ وَالزِّيَادَةُ بِحَقِّهِ مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ الْمِيرَاثِ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ نَصِيبِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي التَّرَكَةِ دَيْنٌ عَلَى النَّاسِ فَأَدْخَلُوهُ فِي الصُّلْحِ عَلَى أَنْ يُخْرِجُوا الْمُصَالِحَ عَنْهُ وَيَكُونَ الدَّيْنُ لَهُمْ فَالصُّلْحُ بَاطِلٌ وَإِنْ شَرَطُوا أَنْ يَبْرَأَ الْغُرَمَاءُ مِنْهُ وَلَا يَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِمْ بِنَصِيبِ الْمُصَالِحِ فَالصُّلْحُ جَائِزٌ قَالَ: صَالَحَتِ امْرَأَةُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ مِنْ نَصِيبِهَا رُبُعَ الثَّمَنِ عَلَى ثَمَانِينَ أَلْفًا وَهَذَا مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى أَنَّهَا كَانَتْ عَارِفَةً بِمِقْدَارِ نَصِيبِهَا. وَجْهٌ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ "وَإِذَا كَانَتِ التَّرَكَةُ بَيْنَ وَرَثَةٍ" أَوْ قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَتَخَارَجَ الشَّرِيكَانِ فَيَأْخُذَ هَذَا دَيْنًا وَهَذَا عَيْنًا فَإِنْ تَوِيَ لِأَحَدِهِمَا لَمْ يَرْجِعْ عَلَى صَاحِبِهِ. (صحيح البخاري، باب الصلح بين الغرماء وأصحاب الميرات والمجازفة في ذلك، رقم 2709). وَجْهٌ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ "وَإِنْ شَرَطُوا أَنْ يَبْرَأَ الْغُرَمَاءُ مِنْهُ" قَالَ شُعْبَةُ عَنِ الْحَكَمِ: هُوَ جَائِزٌ. وَوَهَبَ الْحَسَنُ بْنُ عَلِيٍّ عليهما السلام لِرَجُلٍ دَيْنَهُ. وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ عَلَيْهِ حَقٌّ فَلْيُعْطِهِ أَوْ لِيَتَحَلَّلْهُ مِنْهُ». فَقَالَ جَابِرٌ: قُتِلَ أَبِي وَعَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ فَسَأَلَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم غُرَمَاءَهُ أَنْ يَقْبَلُوا ثَمَرَ حَائِطِي وَيُحَلِّلُوا أَبِي. (صحيح البخاري، باب إذا وهب دينًا على رجل، رقم 2601). أُصُولٌ: أَشْيَاءُ دُو جِنْسٍ كَے ہوں تو سَوْد لازم نہیں آئے گا۔ أَصْلٌ: اِنْكَار کا قَبْضَہ ہو تو صُلْح کے قَبْضَہ کے لئے كَافى ہو گا، اِقْرَار کا قَبْضَہ صُلْح کا قَبْضَہ نہیں ہے جَدِيد ضَرُورِى ہے۔ أَصْلٌ: قَرْض جَب تک وُصُول نہیں ہوا ہے، تو اس کو كسى كا مالك نہیں بنا سكتے ہیں۔ ١٤ أَصْلٌ: جس پر دَيْن تھا اسی کو دَيْن كا مالك بنا دِيا يَعْنِى معاف کر دِيا تو جَائِز ہو گا۔
If the estate is silver and they give him gold, or gold and they give him silver, it is permissible. And if the shared property is gold and silver and other than that, and they settle with him for silver or gold, then it is necessary that what they give him be more than his share of that type, so that his share is like it, and the excess is his right from the rest of the inheritance. So it must be more than his share. And if there is a debt upon people in the estate, and they include it in the settlement on condition that they discharge the one settling from it and the debt becomes theirs, then the settlement is void. And if they stipulate that the creditors are free from it and they do not revert to them for the share of the settler, then the settlement is permissible. He said: The wife of 'Abd al-Rahman settled from her share [being] a quarter of an eighth for eighty thousand, and this is understood as her being aware of the amount of her share. Evidence (2): The saying of the Companion to establish: "And when the estate is among heirs" or Ibn 'Abbas said: There is no harm if two partners separate, one taking a debt and the other taking an asset, and if one of them loses, he does not revert to his partner. (Bukhari) Evidence (1): The hadith to establish: "And if they stipulate that the creditors are free from it" – Shu'bah narrated from al-Hakam: It is permissible. And al-Hasan ibn 'Ali gifted his debt to a man. And the Prophet said: "Whoever has a right owed to him, let him give it or let him seek release from it." Jabir said: My father was killed and he owed a debt, so the Prophet asked his creditors to accept the fruit of my garden and release my father. (Bukhari) Principles: When items are of two types, riba is not required. Principle: If possession is by denial, it suffices for possession in sulh; possession by acknowledgment is not possession in sulh – new possession is necessary. Principle: As long as a debt has not been collected, one cannot make someone else its owner. Principle 14: Making the debtor the owner of the debt, i.e., forgiving it, is permissible.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Sulh (Compromise) in inheritance. It begins by stating the ruling: if the estate consists of a single type (silver or gold) and the heirs give the settling party the other type (gold instead of silver or vice versa), the sulh is valid. The reason is that when the estate is homogenous, giving a different type is treated as a sale of that type for the equivalent, and since the amount given equals the share, it is valid. However, if the estate is mixed (gold, silver, and other items) and the heirs settle with the party for a specific type (silver or gold), then the amount given must exceed his share of that same type. The excess is his share from the rest of the estate. This is because his share includes other species, so the compensation must account for that. If the estate includes a debt owed to the deceased, and the heirs include the debt in the settlement on condition that they discharge the settlor from the debt and keep the debt for themselves, the sulh is void. The reason is that the debt is not yet collected, and transferring it in sulh is like selling a debt, which is not permissible before receipt. But if they stipulate that the creditors (meaning the settlor is free from the debt) and they do not revert to him for his share, the sulh is valid. The passage then cites a historical case from the Companion 'Abd al-Rahman's wife to illustrate that the settling party must be aware of her share. The hadith evidence from Ibn 'Abbas supports the permissibility of partners separating, one taking a debt and the other an asset, without recourse if one loses. Additional hadith from al-Hasan ibn 'Ali and Jabir support the permissibility of forgiving debts or reaching a settlement. The Urdu principles summarize key fiqh points: (1) When items are of different types, riba (usury) is not required; (2) Possession based on denial (munkir) suffices for sulh, but possession based on acknowledgment (muqir) requires new possession; (3) A debt cannot be transferred without actual receipt; (4) Forgiving a debt is permissible.

Key Terms
صُلْح (sulh): A contract of compromise to resolve a dispute, often used in inheritance to divide assets.
مُصَالِح (musalih): The person who makes a compromise, often the one receiving a settlement from heirs.
غُرَمَاء (ghurama'): Creditors or the settler's opponents in sulh context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the estate is mixed (gold, silver, and other items), and the heirs settle with the heir for a specific type (silver), what condition is required for the sulh to be valid?
A) The amount of silver given must equal exactly his share of silver from the estate.
B) The amount of silver given must be more than his share of silver from the estate.
C) The amount of silver given must be less than his share of silver from the estate.
D) The amount of silver given can be any amount as long as both parties agree.

Key Takeaway
Sulh in inheritance requires careful consideration of asset types and debts to ensure validity and avoid riba.

The Basic Ruling of Ghasp: Mithli and Qimi Goods
States the core ruling on usurpation with mithli/qimi distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for usurped goods, classify goods as mithli or qimi, and apply the correct compensation for each category.

Core Idea
Usurped goods must be compensated in kind if they have a market equivalent; otherwise, by market value.

This lesson opens the Book of Ghasp (Usurpation) with the fundamental rule on compensation. The text by Imam al-Quduri establishes a critical distinction between mithli goods (those with exact market equivalents) and qimi goods (unique items). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the obligation of daman (liability) that arises from wrongful taking. The passage also provides scriptural proofs grounding this ruling in the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the act discussed is ghasp (usurpation) – taking another's property without right such that the owner's possession is removed. The ruling: it is haram, and if the property perishes in the usurper's hand, compensation is wajib.
The ruling on compensation is the focus of this lesson.
2
Distinguish Mithli from Qimi
Classify the usurped property: if it has a standard market equivalent (mithli), compensation is in kind (mithl); if it is unique (qimi), compensation is by market value (qimah).
Examples of mithli: grains, oils, eggs. Examples of qimi: animals, real estate, antiques.
3
Examine the Quranic Proof
Read the verse (2:188) prohibiting wrongful consumption of wealth. The prohibition implies that one must restore or compensate for property taken wrongfully. This is the primary dalil for the ruling.
The verse's general prohibition is interpreted to include ghasp, making compensation necessary.
4
Analyze the Hadith Proofs
Consider the three hadiths: (a) the stick hadith – return what you took; (b) the broken bowl hadith – replacement in kind; (c) the emancipation of a share hadith – valuation. Each supports the principle of compensation, with the bowl hadith explicitly showing replacement with a like.
These hadiths illustrate the practical application of the mithli/qimi principle.
5
Apply the Rule to a Scenario
Test your understanding: if someone usurps a sheep (qimi) and it dies, he pays its market value. If he usurps a sack of rice (mithli) and consumes it, he must return an equivalent sack of rice.
The classification determines the mode of compensation.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الْغَصْبِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - لَ وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلَ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ ضَمَانُ مِثْلِهِ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مِثْلٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّا لَا مِثْلَ لَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلٌ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ ا ﴿وَلَا تَأْكُلُواْ أَمْوَلَكُم بَيْنَكُم بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتُدْلُوا بِهَا إِلَى الْحُكَامِ لِتَأْكُلُوا فَرِيقًا مِّنْ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ بِالْإِثْمِ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ) (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر 188)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلٌ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ وَمَنْ أَخَذَ عَصَا أَخِيهِ فَلْيَرُدَّهَا " لَمْ يَقُلْ ابْنُ بَشَّارٍ : ابْنَ يَزِيدَ وَقَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابُ مَنْ يَأْخُذُ الشَّيْءَ عَلَى الْمِزَاحِ، نمبر 5003)
ا وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلٌ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ ﴿فَمَنِ اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ فَاعْتَدُواْ عَلَيْهِ بِمِثْلِ مَا اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 أيت، نمبر 194) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلٌ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ كَانَ عِنْدَ بَعْضٍ نِسَائِهِ، فَأَرْسَلَتْ إِحْدَى أُمَّهَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مَعَ خَادِمٍ بِقَصْعَةٍ فِيهَا طَعَامٌ، فَضَرَبَتْ بِيَدِهَا فَكَسَرَتِ الْقَصْعَةَ، فَضَمَّهَا وَجَعَلَ فِيهَا الطَّعَامَ، وَقَالَ: كُلُوا، وَحَبَسَ الرَّسُولَ وَالْقَصْعَةَ حَتَّى فَرَغُوا، فَدَفَعَ الْقَصْعَةَ الصَّحِيحَةَ وَحَبَسَ الْمَكْسُورَةَ»،(بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا كَسَرَ قَصْعَةً أَوْ شَيْئًا لِغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 2481)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ غَصَبَ شَيْئًا مِمَّا لَهُ مِثْلٌ فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، عَنِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَنْ أَعْتَقَ شَقِيصًا مِنْ تَمُلُوكِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ خَلَاصُهُ فِي مَالِهِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ، قُوْمَ الْمَمْلُوكُ قِيمَةَ عَدْلٍ، ثُمَّ اسْتَسْعِيَ غَيْرَ مَشْقُوقٍ عَلَيْهِ . » » ، بخاري شريف، بَابُ تَقْوِيمِ الْأَشْيَاءِ بَيْنَ الشُرَكَاءِ بِقِيمَةِ عَدْلٍ، غبر 2492)
اصول: شریعت میں مالِ محترم کو اس طرح لے لینا کہ اصل مالک کا قبضہ زائل ہو جائے وہ غصب ہے۔ اصول: کسی کا مال غصب کرنا حرام ہے ، اور واپس کرنالازم ہے ، اگر غصب شدہ مال کا مثل موجود ہو تو مثلی ضمان ہی لازم ہو گا۔
Book of Ghasp (Usurpation). He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: And whoever usurps something that has a like, and it perishes in his hand, then upon him is the guarantee of its like if it has a like, and if it is something that has no like, then upon him is its value. Proof: (1) The verse for establishing 'And whoever usurps something that has a like, and it perishes in his hand'... [Quran 2:188] ... Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'And whoever usurps something that has a like, and it perishes in his hand'... 'Whoever takes his brother's stick, let him return it' ... (Sunan Abi Dawud no. 5003). (Second) Proof: (1) The verse ... [Quran 2:194] ... Proof: (2) The hadith ... from Anas ... that the Prophet replaced a broken bowl with a sound one (Bukhari no. 2481). Proof: (3) The hadith ... from Abu Hurairah ... about emancipating a share of a slave (Bukhari no. 2492). Principle: In Shariah, taking a respected property in a way that removes the owner's possession is ghasp. Principle: Usurping someone's property is haram, and it must be returned; if the usurped property has a like, then the guarantee of its like is necessary.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Ghasp (Usurpation) by stating the fundamental ruling on compensation. The text distinguishes between two categories of goods: mithli (those that have exact equivalents, like grains, oils, and other standardised commodities) and qimi (unique goods, like animals, real estate, etc.). If the usurper destroys or loses a mithli item in his possession, he must return its like (mithl). If the item is qimi (no standard like), he must pay its market value. The author then supports this ruling with multiple proofs: one verse from Surah al-Baqarah (188) prohibiting wrongful consumption of wealth, another verse (2:194) on retaliation in like measure, and several hadiths: the hadith of the stick (whoever takes his brother's stick must return it), the hadith of Anas about the broken bowl (the Prophet ordered replacing the broken bowl with a sound one), and the hadith of emancipating a share of a slave (which implies valuation). The Urdu principle at the end defines ghasp as taking another's property without right such that the owner's possession is removed, and stresses that it is haram. The key takeaway: for mithliyat, replacement in kind; for qimiyat, monetary compensation.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Taking another's property without right such that the owner's possession is removed.
مثلي (mithli): Goods that have standard equivalents in the market, like grains, oils, eggs, etc.
قيمي (qimi): Goods that do not have standard equivalents, like animals, real estate, antiques.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone usurps a specific cow and it dies in his hand, what must he pay?
A) Another cow of the same age and breed
B) The market value of the cow at the time it was taken
C) The market value at the time it died
D) Nothing, because the owner lost ownership once it died

Key Takeaway
The mode of compensation for usurped property depends on whether it is mithli (replacement in kind) or qimi (market value).

Scope of Authorization for the Ma'dhun
Rulings on capacity of authorized slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a slave is considered authorized (ma'dhun) and identify which transactions are valid and invalid for him.

Core Idea
An authorized slave can trade freely, but cannot marry, manumit, or give beyond small hospitality.

This lesson covers the foundational rulings of the authorized slave from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. You will learn how permission from the master creates limited commercial capacity, and which acts remain prohibited due to the slave's continued status as property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on a slave given general permission? The text says his transactions in all types of trade are valid (jāza).
Focus on the phrase 'إذنا عاما' (general permission).
2
Note the exceptions
Which transactions are explicitly prohibited? Marriage, kitāba, manumission for compensation, gifts with or without compensation (except small hospitality).
These are listed after 'وليس له أن يتزوج...'.
3
Understand the rationale
Why are these acts prohibited? Because they affect the master's ownership rights (riqq) and are not within the scope of trading permission.
The slave remains owned property; such acts would diminish the master's property without his consent.
4
Apply to scenarios
Given a specific permission (e.g., for cloth), what can the slave do? The text extends authorization to all related transactions (e.g., buying and selling cloth, pawning cloth).
But permission for a specific item does not make him a ma'dhun.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الْمَأْذُونِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - إِذَا أَذِنَ الْمَوْلَى لِعَبْدِهِ فِي التِّجَارَةِ إِذْنًا عَامًّا جَازَ تَصَرُّفُهُ فِي سَائِرِ التِّجَارَاتِ يَبِيعُ وَيَشْتَرِي يَعْنِي بِمِثْلِ الْقِيمَةِ وَبِنُقْصَانٍ وَيَرْهَنُ وَيَسْتَرْهِنُ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَذِنَ لَهُ فِي نَوْعٍ بِعَيْنِهِ دُونَ غَيْرِهِ فَهُوَ مَأْذُونٌ لَهُ فِي جَمِيعِهَا. وَإِنْ أَذِنَ لَهُ فِي شَيْءٍ بِعَيْنِهِ فَلَيْسَ بِمَأْذُونٍ. وَإِقْرَارُ الْمَأْذُونِ بِالدُّيُونِ وَالْغُصُوبِ جَائِزٌ. وَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ وَلَا أَنْ يُزَوِّجَ مَوَالِيَهُ وَلَا يُكَاتِبُ وَلَا يَعْتِقُ عَلَى مَالٍ وَلَا يَهَبُ بِعِوَضٍ وَلَا بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يُهْدِيَ الْيَسِيرَ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ أَوْ يُضَيِّفَ مَنْ يَصِلُهُ. وَدُيُونُهُ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِرَقَبَتِهِ يُبَاعُ فِيهَا لِلْغُرَمَاءِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَفْدِيَهُ الْمَوْلَى وَيُقْسَمُ ثَمَنُهُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالْحِصَصِ. فَإِنْ فَضَلَ شَيْءٌ مِنْ دُيُونِهِ طُولِبَ بِهِ بَعْدَ الْحَرِيَّةِ. فَإِنْ حَجَرَ عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يَصِرْ مَحْجُورًا عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَظْهَرَ الْحَجْرُ بَيْنَ أَهْلِ سُوقِهِ. فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى أَوْ جُنَّ أَوْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ مُرْتَدًّا صَارَ الْمَأْذُونُ مَحْجُورًا. فَإِنْ أَبَقَ الْعَبْدُ صَارَ مَحْجُورًا. فَإِذَا حَجَرَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِقْرَارُهُ جَائِزٌ فِيمَا فِي يَدِهِ مِنَ الْمَالِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَإِذَا لَزِمَتْهُ دُيُونٌ تُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ وَرَقَبَتِهِ يُبَاعُ فِيهَا. وَإِذَا بَاعَ مِنَ الْمَوْلَى شَيْئًا بِمِثْلِ قِيمَتِهِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ جَازَ وَإِنْ بَاعَهُ بِنُقْصَانٍ لَمْ يَجُزْ. وَإِنْ بَاعَهُ الْمَوْلَى شَيْئًا بِمِثْلِ الْقِيمَةِ أَوْ أَقَلَّ جَازَ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَيْهِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الثَّمَنِ بَطَلَ الثَّمَنُ وَإِنْ أَمْسَكَهُ فِي يَدِهِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ جَازَ. وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الْمَوْلَى الْعَبْدَ الْمَأْذُونَ وَعَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ فَعِتْقُهُ جَائِزٌ.
Book of the Authorized Slave. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - When the master gives his slave general permission to trade, his transactions in all types of trade are valid: he may sell and buy, i.e., at market price or at a loss, he may give and take in pledge. And if he permitted him for a specific type without other, he is authorized for all of them. And if he permitted him for a specific thing, he is not authorized. The acknowledgment of the authorized slave for debts and usurpations is valid. He may not marry nor marry off his masters, nor enter into a kitaba contract, nor manumit for compensation, nor give a gift with or without compensation, unless he gives a small gift of food or hosts someone who visits him. His debts are attached to his person; he is sold for them to creditors unless the master ransoms him, and his price is divided among them in proportion. If anything remains of his debts, he is pursued after manumission. If the master places him under interdiction, he does not become interdicted until the interdiction is announced among the people of his market. If the master dies, or becomes insane, or joins the abode of war as an apostate, the authorized slave becomes interdicted. If the slave absconds, he becomes interdicted. When he is placed under interdiction, his acknowledgment is valid regarding the wealth in his hand according to Abu Hanifah. When debts encompass his wealth and his person, he is sold for them. When he sells something to the master at its value or more, it is valid; if he sells at a loss, it is not valid. If the master sells him something at the value or less, it is valid; if he hands it over to him before receiving the price, the price becomes void, but if he retains it until he collects the price, it is valid. When the master manumits the authorized slave while he has debts, his manumission is valid.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of the Authorized Slave from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It presents a series of rulings (ahkam) on the legal capacity of a slave whom the master has permitted to trade (al-'abd al-ma'dhun). The rulings proceed logically: 

1. General vs. specific permission: If the master gives general permission (idhn 'aamm) for trade, the slave may conduct all types of commercial transactions—buying, selling, pawning, etc.—at market price or even at a loss (indicating the master bears the risk). If the master specifies a particular type of trade (e.g., only cloth), the authorization extends to all related transactions (e.g., buying and selling cloth, pawning cloth) because the permission is understood to include necessary means. However, if the master permits a specific item (e.g., selling this one garment), the slave is not considered authorized for general trade. 

2. Acknowledgment: The authorized slave's acknowledgment of debts (iqrar bi al-duyun) or wrongful taking (ghasb) is valid and binding on his person, as he is trusted in commercial dealings. 

3. Restrictions: Despite his trade authorization, the slave cannot marry himself or others, enter into a kitaba contract (contract of gradual manumission), manumit for a price, or give gifts (hiba) without consideration. He may only give trivial hospitality (diyafah) or small gifts of food to visitors—this is a customary concession for trade relations. The rationale is that these acts affect the master's ownership (riqq) and are outside the scope of trading permission. 

4. Debt attachment: The slave's debts are tied to his person (raqabah); if debts exceed his trade capital, he can be sold by creditors to satisfy them, unless the master pays (fidyah) to free him. The proceeds from his sale are distributed proportionally among creditors. If some debt remains after sale, the slave is pursued for it after he becomes free (e.g., after manumission). 

5. Interdiction (hajr): The master can place the authorized slave under interdiction (hajr) to revoke his permission, but this only takes effect when publicly announced in the marketplace. The slave's status changes automatically if the master dies, becomes insane, or apostatizes and flees to enemy territory; also if the slave himself absconds (iba'). During interdiction, Abu Hanifa holds that the slave's acknowledgment of debt is still valid regarding property in his hands. 

6. Insolvency: When debts exceed the slave's assets and his value, he is sold as a slave to pay creditors. 

7. Transactions with the master: The slave may sell to the master at fair price or higher; selling at a loss is invalid (protecting the master). The master may sell to the slave at fair price or lower; if the master delivers the item before receiving payment, the price is waived (void). But if the master holds the item until paid, the sale is valid. 

8. Manumission: If the master frees the authorized slave while he has debts, the manumission is valid (the slave becomes free), but the debts remain; the slave is then sold to creditors if needed, as per the prior ruling.

The passage is a typical Hanafi matn: concise, rule-based, without proofs. The later commentaries (shuruh) add hadith and rational evidence.

Key Terms
الْمَأْذُونُ (al-ma'dhūn): A slave whom the master has given permission to engage in trade, thereby granting limited legal capacity for commercial transactions.
الْحَجْرُ (al-ḥajr): Legal interdiction preventing the slave from further transactions; effective only upon public announcement in his market.
الْإِقْرَارُ (al-iqrār): Acknowledgment of a debt or liability; valid from an authorized slave regarding trade-related obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts is valid (jā'iz) for an authorized slave with general permission?
A) Giving a gift of a house to a friend.
B) Marrying a free woman.
C) Selling goods at a loss to a third party.
D) Manumitting a fellow slave for a price.

Key Takeaway
The authorized slave's trade capacity is broad but excludes acts affecting his master's ownership rights, such as marriage, manumission, and gifts beyond trivial hospitality.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Debts, Interdiction, and Transactions with the Master
Rulings on debts, hajr, and master transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how debts of the authorized slave are collected, when interdiction becomes effective, and the rules for transactions between the slave and his master.

Core Idea
The slave's debts are secured by his person, interdiction requires public announcement, and sales with the master have special loss protections.

This lesson continues the rulings on the authorized slave, covering debt collection, the process of interdiction (hajr), special rules for sales between slave and master, and the effect of manumission on existing debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on debt attachment
The text says debts are attached to the slave's person (رقبته) and he is sold to pay them. Understand the sequence: if debts exceed assets, the slave can be sold.
Creditors can force sale unless the master ransoms (يفديه).
2
Determine the effective interdiction
Interdiction (hajr) by the master only takes effect when announced in the marketplace. Also, automatic interdiction occurs on master's death, insanity, apostasy, or slave's absconding.
Note the exception: Abu Hanifa holds that even after hajr, the slave's iqrar is valid regarding property in hand.
3
Apply rules for sales between slave and master
The slave may sell to the master at value or higher; selling at a loss is invalid. The master may sell to the slave at value or lower; if he delivers before payment, the price is void.
These rules protect the master from loss and the slave from unfair deals.
4
Understand effect of manumission on debts
If the master frees the authorized slave while he has debts, the manumission is valid, but debts remain; the freed slave can be pursued after freedom.
Manumission does not cancel debts.

Commentary

2. Acknowledgment: The authorized slave's acknowledgment of debts (iqrar bi al-duyun) or wrongful taking (ghasb) is valid and binding on his person, as he is trusted in commercial dealings. 

3. 4. Debt attachment: The slave's debts are tied to his person (raqabah); if debts exceed his trade capital, he can be sold by creditors to satisfy them, unless the master pays (fidyah) to free him. The passage is a typical Hanafi matn: concise, rule-based, without proofs. The later commentaries (shuruh) add hadith and rational evidence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Valid Interdiction of the Ma'dhun
Ruling on the condition of public notification for hajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid hajr on a ma'dhun and explain why public notification is required.

Core Idea
No hajr without public announcement — the ma'dhun's trading rights remain until the market knows.

In Hanafi fiqh, a slave permitted to trade (ma'dhun) can be interdicted (mahjur) by his master, but the interdiction does not take effect automatically. This lesson examines the textual ruling that the master's act of hajr requires public manifestation among the people of the slave's market. Without this, the ma'dhun continues to transact validly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the master placing a hajr on the ma'dhun. The ruling is that the hajr does not take effect until it is manifested among the people of his market.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is 'zuhur al-hajr' (manifestation of the interdiction) among the trading community.
3
Understand the rationale
Why is public notification necessary? To protect third parties (creditors) who dealt with the ma'dhun in good faith.
4
Contrast with automatic hajr
Note that some events cause automatic hajr without such notification (covered in next lesson).

Source Text

فَإِنْ فَضَلَ شَيْءٍ مِنْ دُيُونِهِ طُولِبَ بِهِ بَعْدَ الْخَرِيَّةِ فَإِنْ حَجَرَعَلَيْهِ لَمْ يَصِرْ مَحْجُورًا عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَظْهَرَالْحَجْرُ بَيْنَ أَهْلِ سُوقِهِ فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى أَوْجُنَّ أَوْحَقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ مُرْتَدَّا صَارَ الْمَأْذُونُ مَحْجُورًا لا فَإِنْ أَبَقَ الْعَبْدُ صَارَ مَحْجُورًا فَإِذَا حَجَرَعَلَيْهِ فَإِقْرَارُهُ جَائِزٌ فِيمَا فِي يَدِهِ مِنْ الْمَالِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ
If something remains of his debts, he is pursued for it after the destruction. If his master places him under interdiction, he does not become interdicted until the interdiction is manifested among the people of his market. If the master dies, or becomes insane, or becomes an apostate and joins the abode of war, the ma'dhun becomes interdicted. If the slave absconds, he becomes interdicted. When he is interdicted, his confession regarding what is in his hand of property is valid according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from the Kitab al-Ma'dhun states rulings on the interdiction (hajr) of the permitted slave (al-'abd al-ma'dhun). First, if after the slave's property is used for debts, any remainder of the debt is pursued against him personally after his commercial property is exhausted (al-khariyyah). Second, if the master wishes to place him under interdiction, it does not take effect until it is publicly announced in his marketplace so that potential creditors become aware. Third, certain events automatically cause the slave to become interdicted: the master's death, insanity, or apostasy and joining the enemy's land (dar al-harb), as well as the slave's own flight (abaq). Fourth, while under interdiction, the slave's confession (iqrar) regarding any property in his possession is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, meaning his acknowledgment of debt or ownership is effective for that property. The passage does not provide proof here, but later footnotes cite athar from tabi'un supporting some rulings.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): The slave permitted by his master to engage in trade.
الحجر (al-hajr): Interdiction; legal restriction on the slave's capacity to transact.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession; the slave's acknowledgment of a right or debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately upon the master's decision

C) Upon the slave's knowledge
D) After a judge's confirmation

Key Takeaway
A master's interdiction of a ma'dhun is not effective until it is publicly announced in the slave's market.

Automatic Interdiction of the Ma'dhun
Lists events causing automatic hajr without master's action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the events that automatically make a ma'dhun mahjur without the master's action.

Core Idea
Death, insanity, apostasy of the master, or the slave's own flight trigger automatic hajr.

While a master may proactively interdict a ma'dhun with public notice, certain events automatically sever the permission and render the slave interdicted. This lesson identifies those events from the text: the master's death, insanity, apostasy and joining dar al-harb, and the slave's own flight (abaq). Understanding these automatic triggers is crucial for determining third-party rights and debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the events
List the four events mentioned: master's death, master's insanity, master's apostasy with joining abode of war, slave's flight.
2
Understand the rationale
Each event removes the master's control or the slave's accessibility, thus the permission necessarily ends.
Death terminates ownership; insanity removes capacity; apostasy and flight sever the relationship.
3
Compare with proactive hajr
Automatic hajr requires no public notification — it takes effect immediately upon the event.
Contrast with the condition of public notice for proactive hajr from the previous lesson.
4
Apply to scenarios
Determine the status of transactions occurring after the event but before knowledge.
Good faith of creditors? The school treats these as invalid ab initio.

Validity of the Mahjur Slave's Confession
Ruling on the validity of iqrar of a mahjur slave, with attribution to Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a mahjur slave's confession and identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A mahjur slave's confession regarding property in his hand is valid only according to Abu Hanifa.

When a ma'dhun becomes interdicted, his capacity to transact is restricted, but can he still confess to debts or ownership? The passage states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, his iqrar (confession) regarding property in his possession is valid. This lesson examines the ruling, notes the intra-Hanafi difference, and explores the legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text says: 'When he is interdicted, his confession regarding what is in his hand of property is valid according to Abu Hanifa.' This is the explicit ruling.
2
Identify the scope
The confession is valid only 'fima fi yadihi min al-mal' — regarding property in his actual possession. It does not extend to property that was in his hand before hajr but is no longer there.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
The text attributes this view to Abu Hanifa, implying that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) may disagree or have a nuanced position. In other sources, the Sahibayn hold that the confession is not valid during hajr because the slave's capacity is entirely suspended.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
According to the pre-populated analytical toolbox, Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position. This means in fatwa, the confession of a mahjur slave is accepted for property in his hand.
5
Apply to a scenario
A mahjur slave admits that half of the goods in his shop belong to a partner. According to Abu Hanifa, this confession is binding and must be honored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If the master dies, or becomes insane, or becomes an apostate and joins the abode of war, the ma'dhun becomes interdicted. If the slave absconds, he becomes interdicted. When he is interdicted, his confession regarding what is in his hand of property is valid according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary

Fourth, while under interdiction, the slave's confession (iqrar) regarding any property in his possession is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, meaning his acknowledgment of debt or ownership is effective for that property. The passage does not provide proof here, but later footnotes cite athar from tabi'un supporting some rulings.

Slave's Debts and Sale with Master: Conditions of Validity
Ruling on ma'dhun's sales to master when debts exceed total assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a ma'dhun slave's sale to his master is valid or invalid, and apply these rules to a new scenario.

Core Idea
When a slave's debts exceed his total assets, selling to the master at a loss is invalid because it harms creditors.

This passage from Al-Quduri deals with a special situation: a ma'dhun slave (one permitted to trade) whose debts have become so large that they cover both his property and his person (his market value). In such a case, the law protects the creditors from any collusion between the slave and his master that would reduce the assets available to repay debts. The rulings here ensure that inter-master-slave transactions are at fair market value or better for the creditors' interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage applies 'when debts encompass his property and his person' — meaning the slave's total liabilities equal or exceed the sum of his owned property plus his market value (raqabah). This triggers special protection for creditors.
The ma'dhun slave is still a slave but allowed to trade; his debts are binding.
2
Distinguish two transaction directions
Separate the case where the slave sells to the master from where the master sells to the slave. The validity conditions differ depending on who is the seller.
The master may attempt to benefit at the expense of creditors; the law blocks that.
3
Apply the price condition for slave-to-master sale
If the slave sells something to the master 'at the equivalent of its value or more', the sale is valid. If he sells 'at a loss' (less than value), it is invalid. This prevents the master from getting assets cheaply and reducing the slave's estate.
Loss is measured against the fair market value (qimah).
4
Apply the price condition for master-to-slave sale
If the master sells something to the slave 'at the equivalent of the value or less', it is valid. The master is allowed to sell cheaply to the slave; that does not harm creditors (the slave's property grows).
The inverse rule: master can sell at or below market.
5
Understand the delivery-before-payment rule
If the master sells and hands over the item before receiving the price, the price becomes void. But if the master keeps the item until he collects the price, it remains valid. This prevents the master from waiving the price by premature delivery.
The master is both seller and creditor; delivery before payment extinguishes the debt unintentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا لَزِمَتْهُ دُيُون تُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ وَرَقَبَتِهِ وَإِذَا بَاعَ مِنْ الْمَوْلَى شَيْئًا بِمِثْلِ قِيمَتِهِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ جَازَ وَإِنْ بَاعَهُ بِنُقْصَانٍ لَمْ يَجْزْ وَإِنْ بَاعَهُ الْمَوْلَى شَيْئًا بِمِثْلِ الْقِيمَةِ أَوْ أَقَلَّ جَازَ فَإِنْ سَلَّمَهُ إِلَيْهِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الثَّمَنِ بَطَلَ الثَّمَنُ وَإِنْ أَمْسَكَهُ فِي يَدِهِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي الثَّمَنَ جَازَ
And when debts that encompass his property and his person become binding upon him, and when he sells something to the master for the equivalent of its value or more, it is permissible; but if he sells it to him at a loss, it is not permissible. And if the master sells something to him for the equivalent of the value or less, it is permissible; if he hands it over to him before taking possession of the price, the price becomes void; but if he holds it in his hand until he receives the price, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on the ma'dhun's debts. It states that when the slave is burdened by debts that encompass both his property (mal) and his person (raqabah) — meaning the debts equal or exceed his total value (property + himself) — then special rules apply. The text then gives rules for sales between the slave and his master: (1) If the slave sells something to the master for the fair market value or more, the sale is valid. (2) If he sells at a loss, it is invalid — to protect creditors' interests. (3) If the master sells to the slave at fair value or less, it is valid. (4) A specific scenario: if the master delivers the sold item to the slave before receiving the price, the price obligation is cancelled (since the master is both creditor and seller). But if the master retains the item until he collects the price, the sale remains valid. These rules ensure that the master does not unfairly deplete the slave's assets to the detriment of other creditors.

Key Terms
الرقبة (al-raqabah): The slave's person value; along with his property it forms the total asset base for creditors.
القيمة (al-qimah): Fair market value of the item being sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a ma'dhun slave (with debts encompassing his assets) sells an item to his master for less than its market value, the sale is:
A) Valid, because the master is allowed to benefit from his slave.
B) Invalid, because it harms other creditors.
C) Valid only if the master pays immediately.
D) Suspended until creditors approve.

Key Takeaway
When a ma'dhun slave's debts exceed his total assets, any sale from him to his master at a loss is invalid, while the master may sell at a loss; premature delivery by the master voids the price.

Ruling on Freeing an Indebted Ma'dhun Slave
Ruling on manumission of indebted ma'dhun slave with dissenting view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the manumission of an indebted ma'dhun slave and explain why the slave may be sold for debt.

Core Idea
Manumission is valid but debts survive—slave can be sold and freedman remains liable.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a crucial intersection of slave law and debt. When a master frees a ma'dhun who owes debts, does manumission extinguish those debts? The Hanafi ruling balances the validity of manumission with creditor rights, allowing the slave to be sold for debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is manumission of a ma'dhun slave who has debts. The ruling: manumission is valid (ja'iz).
2
State the Hanafi position on sale
The text states the slave is sold for his debt, even if debts exceed his value. This is the Hanafi position.
3
Note the dissenting view
Al-Tawri and Ibn Abi Layla hold that the slave is not sold. Understand the ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the consequence for remaining debt
After sale, any unpaid debt is pursued against the freedman. Manumission does not discharge debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَعْتَقَ الْمَوْلَى الْعَبْدَ الْمَأْذُونَ وَعَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ فَعِتْقُهُ جَائِزٌ يُبَاعُ الْعَبْدُ فِي دَيْنِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ أَكْثَرُ مِنْ قِيمَتِهِ، وَيَقُولُ: كَمَا ذَهَبُوا بِهِ فَلْيَسْتَسْعَوْهُ قَالَ التَّوْرِيُّ: وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي لَيْلَى: «لَا يُبَاعُ» وَمَا بَقِيَ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ يُطَالَبُ بِهِ الْمُعْتَقُ بَعْدَ الْعِتْقِ
And when the master frees the ma'dhun slave while he has debts, his manumission is valid. The slave is sold for his debt, even if it is more than his value. And he says: 'Just as they have taken him, let them seek payment from him.' Al-Tawri said: And Ibn Abi Layla said: 'He is not sold.' And whatever remains of the debt is pursued against the freedman after manumission.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage deals with a ma'dhun who owes debts at the time of manumission. The ruling: the manumission (itq) is valid and effective — the slave becomes free. However, he may be sold (by the creditors or by the court) to pay off his debts, even if the debts exceed his value. The phrase 'as they have taken him, let them seek payment from him' likely means creditors can pursue the freed slave for the excess. A dissenting view from al-Tawri and Ibn Abi Layla states that the slave should not be sold at all. The passage continues on page 467: whatever debt remains after the sale of the slave is pursued against the freedman after his manumission. This shows that manumission does not extinguish debts; the freed slave remains liable for residual debt.

Key Terms
العتق (al-'itq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave, valid even when slave is indebted.
الاستسعاء (al-istis'a'): The pursuit of the freedman for payment; he may be required to work to pay the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when a ma'dhun is freed while indebted:
A) All debts are extinguished
B) The slave cannot be sold for debt
C) The slave may be sold for debt and any remainder follows the freedman
D) The master must pay the debts

Key Takeaway
Manumission of an indebted ma'dhun is valid, but the slave may be sold to pay debts, and any remaining debt follows the freedman.

Interdiction of the Female Ma'dhun by Giving Birth
Ruling that birth of master's child interdicts the slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of a female slave giving birth to her master's child on her trade permission and explain why it is an automatic interdiction.

Core Idea
Becoming an umm walad automatically revokes the ma'dhun's permission to trade.

This short but important ruling illustrates how a change in legal status can instantly affect transactional capacity. When a ma'dhun female slave bears her master's child, she becomes an umm walad, a status that grants her certain protections but also restricts her ability to engage in trade without renewed explicit permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and action
The subject is the 'amah ma'dhunah' (a female slave permitted to trade). The action is giving birth to her master's child.
2
Recognize the legal consequence
The text states 'that is an interdiction upon her' – the birth itself constitutes a hajr (interdiction) that revokes her trade permission automatically.
No court order or additional action is needed.
3
Understand the underlying reason
Upon becoming an umm walad (mother of the master's child), the slave can no longer be sold and gains certain rights. This change in status is incompatible with the open trading capacity granted by the previous permission.
The master must grant new explicit permission if he wishes her to trade again.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, if such a slave concludes a transaction after giving birth without new permission, the transaction is invalid (batil) because she lacked capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَلَدَتْ الْأَمَةُ الْمَأْذُونَهُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَذَلِكَ حَجْرٌ عَلَيْهَا
And if the ma'dhun female slave gives birth from her master, then that is an interdiction upon her.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This brief rule states that when a female slave who has been given permission to trade (ma'dhunah) gives birth to a child fathered by her master, she becomes interdicted (mahjurah). The birth makes her an umm walad (mother of the master's child), which gives her certain rights and protections. One consequence is that her permission to trade is automatically revoked because her status changes — she can no longer be sold and her capacity to transact is restricted. She would need new explicit permission from the master to continue trading. The proof for this is cited from al-Zuhri in the footnote.

Key Terms
أمة مأذونة (amah ma'dhunah): A female slave permitted by her master to engage in trade.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction; automatic revocation of trade permission upon becoming umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a female ma'dhun's trade permission if she gives birth to her master's child?
A) It remains valid
B) It is automatically revoked (hajr)
C) It is suspended until the child is weaned
D) It requires the child's consent

Key Takeaway
Giving birth to the master's child automatically interdicts the ma'dhun slave, revoking her trade permission without any additional action.

Minor's Permitted Trade: The Discerning Minor Condition
Ruling that a discerning minor's trade with guardian's permission is valid like a ma'dhun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a minor's trade with guardian permission and explain why the Shafi'i counter-argument is rejected.

Core Idea
A discerning minor with guardian permission transacts like a ma'dhun slave — partial capacity suffices with oversight.

This passage addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a minor who has not attained puberty engage in valid trade? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, says yes, provided the minor has understanding (tamyiz) and the guardian gives permission. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that a minor lacks legal capacity entirely. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof, the Shafi'i objection, and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The text says that if the guardian permits a minor to trade and the minor understands buying and selling, the minor is like a ma'dhun slave — transactions are valid.
The condition of 'understanding' means the minor must be discerning (mumayyiz).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a minor's trade is void regardless of permission or understanding, because the minor lacks full legal capacity (ahliyyah).
Shafi'i position is based on the principle that a minor cannot be held responsible for contracts.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that minors are not mukallaf (legally responsible) and thus cannot engage in binding transactions.
This is a general principle that applies to all acts requiring legal capacity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that the minor has partial capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' al-qasira) which is complemented by the guardian's permission, making the transaction valid and binding.
The proof includes a hadith (Sunan Nasa'i) about Umar's marriage as a boy with permission, and qiyas to the ma'dhun slave.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, in the Hanafi school guardians can authorize minors to trade, facilitating economic activity; in the Shafi'i school, only the guardian may transact directly.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَذِنَ وَلِي الصَّبِيِّ لِلصَّبِيَّ فِي التِّجَارَةِ فَهُوَ فِي الشَّرَاءِ وَالْبَيْعِ كَالْعَبْدِ الْمَأْذُونِ إذَا كَانَ يَعْقِلُ الْبَيْعَ وَالشَّرَاءَ
And if the guardian of a minor permits the minor in trade, then he is regarding purchase and sale like the ma'dhun slave, provided he understands purchase and sale.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage equates a minor (sabi) who has received permission from his guardian (wali) to the ma'dhun slave. The condition: the minor must have 'aql (understanding) of buying and selling — i.e., he must be discerning (mumayyiz). If so, his transactions are valid and binding. The footnote cites a hadith from Sunan Nasa'i regarding Umar (as a boy) marrying his mother, indicating that a minor's action with guardian permission can be effective. The Urdu notes clarify the dispute: Imam Shafi'i maintains that even with guardian permission, a minor's transactions are invalid because the minor lacks legal capacity. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that if the minor has sufficient understanding and the guardian's permission, the transaction is valid. The rationale: a minor with limited intellect (tamyiz) can avoid harm; the guardian's permission compensates for the deficiency.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
الولي (al-wali): Guardian; the person authorized to manage the minor's affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what condition must a minor meet for his trade with guardian permission to be valid?
A) He must be post-pubescent
B) He must understand buying and selling
C) He must have a written contract
D) He must be at least ten years old

Key Takeaway
A discerning minor with guardian permission can engage in valid trade; the key condition is 'aql (understanding) of the transaction.
